New York Commodity Prices

Executive Yuan Revises and Approves Relief Fund Allocation Plan; Civil Servant Savings Regulations Sent to Central Political Council; Peng Zhaoxian Appointed Member of Shaanxi Provincial Committee and Concurrently Director of the Civil Affairs Department 28

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 225th meeting at 9:00 AM on the 13th. Kong Xiangxi, Wang Shijie, Zhu Jiahua, Huang Musong, and others attended. Vice President Kong chaired the meeting. The following major cases were resolved:

(A) Reporting Matters: (1) A letter from the National Economic Council, reporting to the National Government on the recent handling of flood prevention along the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers. The original text is copied and sent for reference. (2) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs reported that it has lodged a protest with the Japanese Embassy regarding the detention of Tao Shangming.

(B) Reviewing and Reporting Matters: (1) Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Transportation, Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry, Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education, Vice Minister Tao of the acting Ministry of Interior, Director Liu of the National Health Administration, and Vice Minister Zou of the Ministry of Finance jointly reported on the review of the draft Civil Servant Savings Regulations. After modifying the principles and articles, they submitted their revised opinions for consideration. Resolution: Approved the revisions according to the review opinions and sent them to the Central Political Council. (2) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs and Vice Minister Tao of the acting Ministry of Interior reported on the review of the organizational regulations of the administrative inspectorate commissioner's office in Gansu Province. After joint review and participation in discussions by representatives from the Military Affairs Commission, it was deemed that the establishment of administrative inspectors and district security commanders requested by the Gansu Provincial Government could be temporarily approved for record, and the submitted organizational regulations were appropriately revised for consideration. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinions.

(C) Appointments and Removals: (1) Resolution: Shao Lizi, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, is instructed to no longer concurrently serve as Director of the Civil Affairs Department. Peng Zhaoxian is appointed as a member of the Shaanxi Provincial Government and concurrently Director of the Civil Affairs Department. (2) The Military Affairs Commission requested the appointment of Chen Guangzhong as the commander of the 63rd Division of the Army. Resolution: Passed.

(D) Matters for Discussion: (1) Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance and Chairman Xu of the Relief Committee reported on the consultation and distribution of relief funds to various provinces as ordered. Two principles were drafted, and a list of distributed relief funds was submitted for consideration and record. Resolution: Approved with revisions. (Central News Agency dispatch, 13th)

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan passed the distribution of 1 million relief funds consulted by the Ministry of Finance and the Relief Committee on the morning of the 13th, but with slight increases and decreases. The breakdown of funds to various provinces is as follows: Hubei 300,000, Shandong 250,000, Hunan 100,000, Henan and Jiangxi 60,000 each, Anhui 30,000, Hebei and Fujian 20,000 each, Shaanxi, Gansu, Guizhou, and Shanxi 15,000 each, Suiyuan, Ningxia, and Chahar 10,000 each, epidemic prevention 60,000, and Xinjiang epidemic prevention 10,000. (Central News Agency dispatch, 13th)

(Nanjing) The allocation of relief funds for fifteen provinces was passed by the Executive Yuan meeting on the 13th, and will be allocated by the Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Management Committee to the Relief Committee to implement relief efforts in conjunction with the disaster-stricken provinces. The allocated amounts are: Hubei 300,000, Shandong 250,000, Hunan 100,000, Henan and Jiangxi 60,000 each, Hebei 20,000, Anhui 30,000, the remaining 20,000, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Gansu, and Guizhou 15,000 each, Harbin, Suiyuan, Ningxia 10,000 each, and 60,000 for epidemic prevention in the disaster-stricken provinces along the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers, and 10,000 for epidemic prevention in Xinjiang Province, totaling 1 million. (Special dispatch, 13th)

Strong Wind and Rain in Tangshan; Streets and Markets Flooded; Dou River Coal Transport River Swells; Tang-Feng Highway Destroyed 29

(Tianjin) Tangshan experienced heavy rain and hail on the morning of the 11th, exacerbated by a hurricane. The water depth in Grain Market Street and Xinli Street was two feet, and the streets and markets were flooded like a large river. The weather cleared on the afternoon of the 12th. Many houses collapsed. Many electric and telephone lines were also blown down. The Dou River coal transport river overflowed. The Tang-Feng Highway was again submerged and destroyed. The river water is still rising. (Special dispatch, 13th)

(Beiping) The Dou River and Coal Transport River southeast of Tangshan have been rising continuously for days. More than ten sections of the provincial highway between Tangshan and Fengrun have been washed away by the water. Long-distance buses from Tangshan to various places have been suspended since the 12th. The area within dozens of miles of Tangshan City experienced a heavy storm from the 11th. Many electric and telephone lines were cut, and countless houses collapsed, making it an unprecedented disaster. (Special dispatch, 13th)

The Fuyang River Continues to Rise

(Tianjin) The Fuyang River in Handan has risen another two feet. Since late July, it has been raining continuously, and the accumulated water and river water have merged into one. More than 130 villages, including Sucao, Kongqiao, Chengnan, and Liuzhuang, have been flooded again. All the villages are located in the water, and the disaster situation is tragic. (Special dispatch, 13th)

The Yongding River's Flow is Now Stable

(Tianjin) The water level of the Yongding River at Lugouqiao receded by two centimeters on the 13th, and the flow is now stable. The North China Ice Control Association investigated the river and found that it is only ten days away from the end of the flood season. If there is no heavy rain in the coming days, a safe year can be celebrated. (Special dispatch, 13th)

The South Canal is Rising Dangerously

(Tianjin) The South Canal continued to rise sharply on the evening of the 12th, rising several inches. The water level in the first and second sections of Cangxian and Lianzhen reached 18.45 meters, level with the banks, and extremely dangerous. It is difficult to count the number of string holes in Zhangjia Dike and Xiaoquan Dike in Dongguang. If it continues to rise, the entire dike will collapse. The River Bureau has ordered each county to gather more than a thousand laborers to protect and reinforce the dike. Cui Shaoyan, the head of the third section of the River Bureau, carried thousands of sacks from Tianjin on the 13th to fill the holes. (Special dispatch, 13th)

Victims Along the Xiang River Stretch Their Necks Awaiting Relief 30

(Hankou) The Xiang River team of the Provincial Government's Flood Disaster Inspection Group completed its inspection. On the 12th, it arrived in Huayuan by car, and on the 13th, it transferred to the Pinghan Railway to return to Hankou. According to the members of the group, the disaster along the Xiang River is very serious, and many embankments have collapsed. The victims are stretching their necks waiting for relief. The head of the group, Li Shucheng, is said to have drafted a relief and embankment repair plan. Li visited Zhang Qun that evening, reported on the inspection situation, and requested him to quickly repair the collapsed mouths of the Lao Long Dike, hoping to revitalize both industry and agriculture. (Special dispatch, 13th)

Strong Wind and Rain in Wuhan Yesterday 31

(Hankou) Wuhan has been muggy for days. There was a strong wind, thunder, and rain on the 13th, and the weather was slightly cooler. (Special dispatch, 13th)

South Suzhou Station; Freight Car and Coal Car Collide; Traffic Temporarily Blocked but Quickly Restored; Driver Jumps from Car and Saves His Life 34

(Xuzhou) At 2:00 AM on the 13th, the China East coal train on the Tianjin-Pukou southbound line, when it arrived at South Suzhou Station, the driver, Sang Ziqian, drove too fast and drove straight past the station, causing it to collide with the northbound intermodal freight train parked on the second track south of Suzhou Station. Both locomotives were damaged, and one section of the coal train was wrecked. Traffic was temporarily blocked. The Xuzhou Station received the news and rushed to send a rescue train to the scene to lift the cars and clear the tracks, which was quickly repaired. The northbound passenger trains were all delayed that morning and only gradually passed Xuzhou North Station. According to sources, Sang and the freight train driver, Fan Zhuquan, jumped out of the car when the accident occurred and saved their lives. Because it was not a passenger train, no one was injured. The coal locomotive was No. 52, and the freight locomotive was No. 297. (Special dispatch, 13th)

(Jinan) The Tianjin-Pukou coal train derailed at South Suzhou, and the Pingpu train was six hours late arriving in Jinan. (Special dispatch, 13th)

(Nanjing) The petitioning delegation of newspaper journalists from various counties in Jiangsu Province, with [unclear number of] people, departed from the Central Hotel at 7:30 AM on the 13th in six cars carrying petitions and banners. They then went to the Ministry of Interior to petition and were received by Li Songfeng, Director of the Police Administration Department, who said that the Ministry of Interior would do its best to take into account the opinions of the press in the implementation rules of the Publication Law, and at the same time, he sincerely hoped that the Publication Law could be reconsidered. Then, due to time constraints, the delegation split into two groups. Group A went to the Executive Yuan to petition. Because the Executive Yuan was in session, they were received by Secretary-General Zhao Hengrong, who promised to forward their opinions to the President for adoption and strive to facilitate the implementation of the Publication Law. Group B went to the Propaganda Committee of the Central Party Headquarters and were received by Peng Gezhen, Director of the News Section, who promised to convey the various opinions to the Central Political Council. Cheng Cangbo, Bao Mingshu, and others gave speeches. At 2:30 PM, the Central Party Headquarters sent a special car to invite the entire delegation to visit the mausoleum. At 6:00 PM, the Shanghai and New Daily's Beijing offices hosted a public banquet at the Liu Huachun Restaurant. They dispersed at 7:30 PM. The delegation decided to continue petitioning the Judicial Yuan and the Central Political Council on the 14th. Some delegates from afar left Beijing first. The delegation also appointed representatives from Wu County, Xiwu County, and Jin County to organize the Jiangsu Provincial Press Association, which will be established in a short time. Tao Shangming Detained by the Japanese; The Ministry of Foreign Affairs Protests to the Japanese Embassy 36

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has lodged a protest with the Japanese Embassy in China regarding the detention of Tao Shangming, the administrative commissioner of the Mi-Yu District in Hebei Province, and reported to the Executive Yuan meeting on the 13th. The details of Tao's detention are roughly as follows: Liu Zuozhou, the captain of the first battalion of the Hebei Luandong District Security Corps, welcomed the Japanese garrison commander, Umezu, at the Luanzhou Station on the 4th to inspect Yuguan. After Umezu got on the train, he was suddenly assassinated by someone wearing civilian clothes. The Japanese side considered the incident serious. Tao happened to hand over his command on the 3rd, which made the Japanese side suspicious. Tao went to the office of the military attache of the Japanese Embassy in Beijing on the afternoon of the 5th to discuss the Liu case and was detained and transferred to the Japanese Embassy barracks. Banditry Still Rampant in the War Zone 38

(Beiping) According to a telephone call from Zunhua, more than 2,000 bandits were found in Maoshangou, 60 miles northeast of Zunhua County. They were well-equipped with guns and carried small cannons and mortars. In addition to the Special Police First Team led by Zhang Yantian blocking and suppressing them, the county government is mobilizing the entire county's militia to assist in the suppression. The militia gathered at Jinshan Temple, 20 miles northeast of the county, on the 12th, with more than 4,000 people led by the captain-general, Shen Yuexian. According to those familiar with the local situation, Maoshangou is a dangerous area with steep mountains and difficult roads, so the bandits are able to occupy the area and are difficult to eliminate completely in a short time. In addition, there are more than ten bandits hiding in the Kedaotun Nanshan, 50 miles southwest of Zunhua County, all of whom have rifles and pistols and plan to kidnap and extort money in nearby villages. (Special dispatch, 13th)

(Tianjin) More than 600 cavalry bandits from Liu Guitang's forces have changed their target to the fifth district of Yanqing County. Each village has automatically organized a people's self-defense force to confront the bandits. On the night of the 11th, due to the rain, the bandits attacked the crowd fiercely, intending to surround the self-defense force and seize their weapons. After several hours of fierce fighting, the team retreated to Yongning Fort due to a lack of ammunition. Dozens of villages have been occupied by the bandits, and many traitors have joined the bandits, making their momentum very large. The Chahar army has sent security teams to suppress them. (Special dispatch, 13th)

Impressions of a Southern Tour - Our Newspaper's Special Shanghai Reporter Qian Hua 79

(V) Southern Summer Resorts

Hong Kong was originally a barren island. After decades of deliberate management by the British, it has almost all been developed. Roads are built around the mountains, winding and passable. The reporter and Mr. Zhang hired a car to tour the entire Hong Kong Island at sunset. Driving up the hills and winding around the mountains, the peaks are layered and verdant. Looking out at the seaside, fishing boats are silent. There are waterfalls, lakes, secluded trees, and villas. The natural beauty is embellished by artificial touches, as if one is in a painting, reluctant to leave. There is a funicular railway that can go directly to the top of the mountain. From the parking lot at the foot of the mountain to the mountain top station, it is 1,190 feet above sea level. The temperature at the foot of the mountain that day was 92 degrees, and the thermometer at the mountain top station was 78 degrees. A cool breeze was blowing, refreshing the whole body. It takes another 20 minutes to walk to the top, overlooking the entire Hong Kong. The highest point is the British military's fort and military radio station, which is off-limits. Villas are like clouds on the mountain, all inhabited by millionaires or wealthier, where they can recuperate and eliminate all worries. It is truly a famous southern summer resort. At the foot of the mountain there is a very large racetrack and a seaside bathing beach. It is said that Chen Mingshu, Cai Tingkai, and others go to the seaside bathing beach to swim every day.

(VI) What I Saw on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Train

From Hong Kong to Guangzhou, one can take the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway by land, which takes three hours. By water, one can take the Hong Kong-Guangdong steamer, which takes seven hours, but one can enjoy the scenery of the Pearl River along the way. The reporter left Hong Kong at 4:00 PM on the second, took the ferry to Kowloon, and then took the Guangzhou-Kowloon train directly to Guangzhou from Kowloon Station at 4:50 PM. I planned to take the waterway back to Hong Kong from Guangzhou on my return journey so that I could see both land and water, and not be partial. The Guangzhou-Kowloon train is jointly operated by China and Britain. It is clean, stable, and fast, and the timetable is very accurate. There are many mountains along the way, which is very different from the scenery of the Shanghai-Hangzhou and Beijing-Shanghai lines. Looking out the window, more than one-third of the fields along the entire line were flooded. One can imagine the severity of the flood in Guangdong. People in the train said that this was the third major flood, probably affected by the flood in Fujian, coupled with mountain torrents, which were unable to be discharged, resulting in immeasurable losses. We arrived in Guangzhou at 7:45 PM, the lights shone brightly, and the train sounds were loud and noisy. The lively scene was only slightly less than that of Shanghai. It is indeed the largest city in the southwest. The next day, with a friend from Guangzhou as a guide, I hired a car to tour the city, visited the Tomb of the Seventy-Two Martyrs of Huanghuagang, the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Monument, and the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall. The Municipal Government is located in the center of the city, and the architecture is also palatial. Sun Yat-sen Park is located opposite the Municipal Government. The roads are wide and flat, and the Western-style buildings are tall and grand. Guangzhou has all the tools of a modern city. What is even more precious is that Guangzhou is a purely Chinese-built city, and it is on par with the Shanghai and Tianjin concessions. In Shamian, the British and French concessions in Guangzhou, it is secluded in a corner, the situation is dim, and commerce is declining. I sincerely hope that the Greater Shanghai Plan will succeed one day, moving the prosperous streets such as Nanjing Road to the city center, and replicating the changes that have occurred in the Shamian concession today.

Guangzhou Sun Yat-sen Memorial Monument

Western Shandong Province: The Widespread Flooding Continues; Over 100,000 Disaster Victims Sheltered in Various Counties 80

A dispatch from Jinan reports that since the breaches and collapses along the Yellow River in this province, coupled with the continuous influx of floodwaters from Tongguan and Shaanxi, alerts have been frequent since the 8th. On the evening of the 10th, the provincial government chairman, Han Fuqu, received a telegram from Wang Shaochang, the chief administrator of the western Shandong experimental zone, reporting that the upstream floodwaters from Shaanxi Province were surging downwards, and the flow below Liuzhuang was exceptionally turbulent. In Heze County, the Zhukou dangerous section had sufficient stone materials, and due to proactive reinforcement and effective emergency efforts, it had not yet been breached despite being directly hit by the flood. However, at the northern end of the Jiangsu embankment below Zhukou, due to the immense and forceful water, over twenty meters were successively washed away by the rapid current on the evening of the 10th. Consequently, the current became even more rapid. At the old breach in Juancheng County, the floodwaters breached the layers of civilian embankments and government dikes, flowing eastward in two branches from Linpuji. The larger branch headed directly towards the northern border of Heze, already overflowing the newly built civilian embankments in Dehua Township, flooding over the top of the embankments without obstruction. The smaller branch threatened to inundate Yuncheng's southern regions, potentially flooding Niuye and Jiaxiang again. As for the remaining embankment head east of Dongzhuangkou, it was collapsing under the force of the flood, encroaching upon civilian embankments. Emergency repairs had been ongoing for several days, and the situation had become increasingly critical since the day before yesterday. Not only was the remaining embankment still collapsing, but the retaining dike was also sinking. Yesterday (the 11th), the flow did not abate, with the main current closely abutting the southern section of the civilian-built retaining dike, eroding about several tens of zhang (a unit of length). Qin Daoyu and Chen Wenmo, recognizing the critical situation, purchased cash-based earth materials to reinforce the bank and installed support piles and willow bundles, throwing bags to protect the slope. With these emergency measures, the collapse has slightly stabilized. After receiving the report, the River Affairs Bureau, in addition to instructing Qin Daoyu and Chen Wenmo to actively carry out emergency repairs and expedite civilian repairs, also borrowed dragon ropes from the Yellow River Water Conservancy Committee for binding willow branches for protection. Furthermore, the Jiangsu embankment near the Linshengtun outlet, which prevented the entire river from diverting southward after this year's breach, was due to the work of diverting the flow towards the Jiangsu embankment. However, currently, its first embankment is affected by the drainage from the outlet, with an exceptionally fierce current. The fifth, sixth, and seventh groynes are either shifting or being destroyed. Soldiers and laborers from that section are bundling piles to provide protection. Although the ice is receding, the current remains ferocious, and the construction base has collapsed by forty to fifty zhang. As of last night, they were using burlap sacks to throw bricks to reinforce the pressure. According to a telegram from Zhuang Shouzhong, the magistrate of Dong'e County, at 5 PM on the 10th, the Yellow River's water level surged, and the second Niu Tun dam was breached by the powerful current, with a length of eight chi (a unit of length) and a width of one zhang two chi. The fourth dam was also breached, with a length of one zhang and a width of two zhang. The magistrate immediately went to the work site to supervise the laborers and flood prevention chief, Liu Fuyan, in their efforts to install willow branches for emergency protection. The small rivers, flooded by both the Yellow River and the converging water, had long reached their capacity. Now, the Qili River in Heze is being inundated by the large breach from Juancheng flowing through Dehua Township. Due to the substantial volume, several sections of the downstream civilian embankments were breached, directly threatening the northern embankments of the Zhao Wang River. The villages in the northern part of Dingtao County are all feeling the impact of the Yellow River. Ten thousand laborers have been mobilized, joining the twenty thousand laborers in Heze to desperately carry out protective measures. In the Anxingmu area downstream of the river, the Yellow River's floodwaters rose steeply by one meter and seven cun (a unit of length). The higher ground in the vicinity, which initially suffered less damage when the floodwaters first arrived, now has all its villages completely submerged. In Yuncheng County, the Yellow River's water had originally approached the city walls, but fortunately, there was a large protective embankment for defense. However, the water level has now increased by four hua chi (a unit of length), and many leaks have been discovered in the protective embankment, with the Yellow River seeping into the embankment, making the situation critical. If the Juancheng breach water arrives again, it may be difficult to ensure safety, and the county seat will inevitably be flooded. The disaster area is expanding, making the future difficult to predict. The Yellow River's water in Juye has risen another one chi, already reaching the base of the city walls. There is a shortage of piling materials in the city, and boats have been dispatched to neighboring counties for purchase. The houses in the flooded villages, which had not previously collapsed, have now all collapsed due to prolonged submersion. County Magistrate Gong Min is defending the county seat day and night. Also, according to news from Yuncheng, the Songjin River's water level has risen by one chi and five cun from the 10th to the 11th. The protective embankment has repeatedly faced danger, with repairs in one area leading to breaches in another. At 2 AM on the 10th, two breaches occurred simultaneously in the southwest and northeast, and efforts are being made to repair them. The waters of Yutai Lake are overflowing, and news is delayed. As of yesterday, a report from County Magistrate Yang Qidong on the 9th stated that the water level in lakes such as Zhaoyang and Shushan was continuously increasing. The lake embankments north of Wanfu River and south of Ma Pit were completely submerged, and boats could pass through anywhere. After several days and nights of emergency repairs by officials and civilians, the western branch river's eastern bank in Chenwan in the third district, gave way on the afternoon of the 9th when strong winds and waves arose, with two breaches, each several tens of zhang wide. The third district is now indistinguishable from the lake and river, a vast expanse of water. Furthermore, according to a telegram from Jining, the water level in the upper reaches of the Grand Canal, at Dachangou Anju, has risen three cun, while the lower reaches, at Luqiao, have not risen. The water from the breach at Xindian has risen one cun, with no change in area. The water between the Zhao Wang River and the Shu River has risen one cun. Both Shushan Lake and Nanyang Lake have risen one cun. The water in the 12th Transport Depression has decreased by one cun.

The disaster area in western Shandong is expanding daily, with the number of disaster victims reaching five million. The provincial government has established shelters in counties that have not been affected, providing them with accommodation. Later, Wang Shaochang, the chief administrator of the experimental zone, believed that it was difficult to transport disaster victims back and forth, so it would be more convenient to establish shelters directly in the affected counties. Thus, shelters were added in ten counties, including Heze and Dingtao. As of now, the statistics show that the forty-eight shelters in unaffected counties have accommodated 65,417 disaster victims. The number of disaster victims already accommodated within the disaster area is not included. Roughly, it is estimated that there are already more than one hundred thousand people. There are undoubtedly many more who are being transported or who are guarding their property and unwilling to leave. Here is a list of the number of disaster victims accommodated in the forty-eight shelters in the unaffected counties: Jinan City 9,626, Dezhou 1,387, Teng County 1,706, Zou County 815, Qufu 893, Pingyuan 637, Tai'an 1,685, Ziyang 836, Zouping 300, Zhangqiu 2,000, Yidu 2,000, Changshan 1,200, Changle 1,300, Linzi 1,000, Zichuan 1,000, Weixian 1,500, Jiaoxian 1,959, Jimo 1,500, Sishui 600, Gaomi 1,300, Qihe 1,000, Ningyang 1,000, Pingyin 800, Yixian 1,000, Huantai 1,634, Dong'e 1,500, Anqiu 1,583, Jiyang 1,200, Linba 669, Gaoyuan 600, Linqu 1,000, Changyi 1,000, Enxian 1,000, Changqing 1,000, Gaotang 1,000, Deping 800, Yexian 1,500, Lingxian 1,200, Shouguang 1,200, Zhucheng 1,500, Guangrao 1,200, Boshan 1,200, Feicheng 600, Chiping 1,000, Wucheng 1,000, Shanghe 1,200, Pingdu 1,500, Licheng 2,277. The total is 65,417 people. (12th)

Lin'an County: Prohibition of Selling and Smoking Cigarettes

Lin'an County has prohibited the sale and smoking of cigarettes, incorporating this into the Baojia regulations. Cigarette shops in the county, believing that the county magistrate was forcing them to stop business, cutting off their livelihood, submitted a petition to the provincial government for relief. On the occasion of renewing their licenses in the autumn, they still prepared taxes in accordance with the regulations and applied to the county government for cigarette licenses. Currently, more than a dozen households have been approved by the county government. Those who have obtained licenses then requested cigarettes from the Yuhang cigarette distributors. Yesterday (the 8th), cigarette distributors such as Yuhang Chengchang sent partners Zhou Fuxing and Wang Boting, carrying a total of nineteen cartons of various cigarettes to Lin'an. When they arrived at the station, they were seized by the county's security team and police officers stationed at the station and escorted to the county government, then transferred to the town office for punishment. The town mayor did not accept the case, so the chief of the Public Security Section interrogated them and escorted them out of the territory. Local cigarette shops, believing that the county was illegally interfering with their business, sent letters to the Hangzhou Cigarette Industry Association, requesting assistance. The association has separately submitted petitions to the provincial government and the Tax Administration of the Ministry of Finance, requesting that they be dispatched to thoroughly investigate and effectively protect them.

The accumulated profit for the past years is 40,000 yuan. The deposits are 161,000 yuan, the current deposits are 72,000 yuan, the temporary account is 6,000 yuan, the peer debt is 31,000 yuan, the Shanghai foreign market is 30,000 yuan, the Ningbo foreign market is 70,000 yuan, and the debt is 284,000 yuan. The bank still has a surplus between its receipts and payments. Because depositors have difficulty in withdrawing cash, it had no choice but to announce liquidation yesterday.

Local News

Stamp Tax Law Officially Implemented on September 1st; The Legislative Yuan, Considering the Difficulties of Business, Reduced the Tax Rate; Provisional Regulations and Other Provisions Simultaneously Abolished; The Ministry of Finance Informs the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the General Chamber of Commerce 81

The Stamp Tax Law, which was drafted by the Legislative Yuan last year and promulgated by the National Government, had several tax rates that were higher than the provisional regulations. Various sectors requested the Legislative Yuan to amend it. The Legislative Yuan has now accommodated the request, amended the articles, and reduced the tax rate. The Executive Yuan has decided that it will be officially implemented from September 1st of this year. All provisional stamp tax regulations, single-line rules of various provinces, and all precedents previously approved by the Ministry of Finance for exemption, delayed payment, or reduced stamp tax will be simultaneously abolished. The details are as follows:

Telegram from the Ministry of Finance

The Ministry of Finance believes that the implementation of the Stamp Tax Law is imminent. In addition to instructing the Tax Administration to instruct its subordinates to comply, it also sent telegrams to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the National General Chamber of Commerce to inform them. The original telegram stated, "The Stamp Tax Law was promulgated by the National Government on December 8, 1934. According to Article 24 of the original law, the date of implementation will be determined by order. Now, the National Government has ordered, 'The Stamp Tax Law will be implemented from September 1, 1935.' The implementation rules have also been drafted in detail by the Ministry in accordance with Article 23 of the original law, 'The implementation rules of this law shall be determined by the Ministry of Finance,' a total of 19 articles, and stipulates in Article 19 that these implementation rules shall be implemented on the same day as the Stamp Tax Law. They were promulgated by the Ministry Order on July 23 of this year, and submitted to the Executive Yuan and the National Government for record. After the Stamp Tax Law and the implementation rules are implemented on September 1 of this year, all provisional stamp tax regulations, single-line rules of various provinces, and all precedents previously approved by the Ministry for exemption, delayed payment, or reduced stamp tax should be abolished uniformly. However, soda water is a commodity tax and is different from the certificate tax. The method should be formulated and handled separately. In addition to issuing orders for announcements separately, the Stamp Tax Law and the implementation rules of the Stamp Tax Law, each 50 copies, will be sent to the provincial stamp and alcohol tax bureaus for distribution to local chambers of commerce and dissemination to merchants for reference. The above tax law and implementation rules, 50 copies each, are hereby sent to your association for reference and use." Ministry of Finance Stamp.

Reduced Tax Rate

Articles 1, 2, and 3 of Article 16 of the Stamp Tax Law, the original tax rates for invoices, receipts for money and goods, and bills, etc., started at three yuan and increased progressively according to the cumulative method, up to a maximum of one yuan. Later, various sectors believed that they could not afford it, and requested amendments. After reconsideration by the Legislative Yuan, it was approved to reduce it to alleviate business difficulties. The amended articles and tax rates are recorded as follows: (1) Invoices (all documents issued by various industry shops after the sale of goods, listing the name, quantity or price, are included) Each invoice, if the price of the goods is more than three yuan, affix one cent of stamp tax; if it is more than ten yuan, affix two cents of stamp tax; if it is more than one hundred yuan, affix three cents of stamp tax. (2) Receipts for money and goods (all documents established after receiving money or goods are included, except for deposit receipts from the financial industry) Each receipt, if the amount or price of the goods is more than three yuan, affix one cent of stamp tax; if it is more than ten yuan, affix two cents of stamp tax; if it is more than one hundred yuan, affix three cents of stamp tax. (3) Bills (all documents listed by hotels, restaurants or other industrial and commercial businesses that should be paid and given to customers as payment documents are included) Each bill, if the amount is more than three yuan, affix one cent of stamp tax; if it is more than ten yuan, affix two cents of stamp tax; if it is more than one hundred yuan, affix three cents of stamp tax.

Implementation Rules

Article 1: These implementation rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 23 of the Stamp Tax Law. Article 2: The cooperative mentioned in Article 3, paragraph 6 of the Stamp Tax Law refers to a cooperative established in accordance with the Cooperative Law. Article 3: The copy and transcript mentioned in Article 3, paragraph 7 of the Stamp Tax Law shall have the same content as the original with affixed stamp tax, and are only for reference. Article 4: The so-called internally used single documents mentioned in Article 4 refer to those used for internal notification within the agency or organization. Mutual use between branch agencies and the head agency or between branch organizations and the head organization shall not be regarded as internally used. Article 5: The bill for requesting payment mentioned in Article 3, paragraph 9 of the Stamp Tax Law refers to a bill that only lists the amount of arrears for the year. The bill listing the name, quantity, and price issued to customers monthly or annually according to custom, such as the bill of a clothing store, shall not be regarded as a bill for requesting payment. The bill for checking numbers mentioned in the same article refers to a document issued by the store to the trading account at the end of each month or year to check whether there are errors in the number of receipts and payments, such as the monthly statement of the silver and money industry. Article 6: According to Article 5 of the Stamp Tax Law, the documents that should be affixed with stamp tax shall be affixed with stamp tax tickets before delivery or use. If, due to special circumstances, the Ministry of Finance approves the use of other methods instead of affixing stamp tax tickets, the effect shall be the same. Article 7: According to the provisions of Article 10 of the Stamp Tax Law, the person using the documents concluded abroad shall be responsible for affixing the stamp tax tickets. Article 8: When government offices, schools, or public or private groups affix and stamp stamp tax tickets on the documents issued in accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the Stamp Tax Law, they shall first verify whether the stamp tax tickets affixed are sufficient and whether they have been torn off and reused, and correct them at any time. If they do not correct them and stamp them, the person stamping them shall be responsible for the illegal punishment. Article 9: The words "such as so-and-so" mentioned in the remarks column of the tax rate table in Article 16 of the Stamp Tax Law are examples of the documents of this paragraph. All those that are not listed but whose nature is the same as the nature of the documents of this paragraph shall still affix stamp tax tickets in accordance with the tax rate of this paragraph. If the nature cannot be determined, it shall be handled by the Ministry of Finance. Article 10: Regardless of when it starts to be used, the validity of the stamp tax tickets affixed to the various books that should be affixed with stamp tax in accordance with the Stamp Tax Law shall expire at the end of the year, the commercial general closing date. If the accounts are closed in accordance with the fiscal year, they shall expire at the end of the fiscal year. If they continue to be used after the expiration date, stamp tax tickets shall be affixed separately. Article 11: The books compiled in loose-leaf form shall still be affixed with stamp tax tickets in accordance with the book example. Article 12: If the various tickets that should be affixed with stamp tax in accordance with the Stamp Tax Law are ordered into a book style, in addition to affixing stamp tax tickets for each piece in accordance with the law before use or delivery, it is not necessary to affix stamp tax tickets on the book in accordance with the book example. Article 13: The words "more than three yuan, ten yuan, one hundred yuan" mentioned in the nature column of the tax rate table in Article 16 of the Stamp Tax Law are all calculated together with this book. For example, if the price of goods on an invoice is more than three yuan, one cent of stamp tax shall be affixed; if it is more than ten yuan, two cents of stamp tax shall be affixed; if it is more than one hundred yuan, three cents of stamp tax shall be affixed, and so on. Article 14: The words "excluding deposit receipts from the financial industry" in the nature column of Article 2 of the tax rate table in Article 16 of the Stamp Tax Law are because deposit receipts from the financial industry belong to the deposit documents exemplified in the remarks column of Article 4, and stamp tax tickets shall be affixed in accordance with the tax rate specified in Article 4, and the tax rate specified in Article 2 shall not be applied. Article 15: The savings deposit mentioned in Article 9 of the tax rate table in Article 16 of the Stamp Tax Law shall be limited to those issued by the savings business established in accordance with the Savings Bank Law. Article 16: According to Article 18 of the tax rate table in Article 16 of the Stamp Tax Law, there is no provision for exemption from affixing stamp tax for documents of joint venture operations that are less than a certain amount. Stamp tax tickets shall still be affixed for each piece with an amount of less than one hundred yuan. Article 17: In accordance with the provisions of Article 20 of the Stamp Tax Law, when determining fines separately, if each piece is in accordance with the provisions of Article 18, paragraph 1, the number of punishments is less than three yuan, it shall be determined in accordance with the provisions of Article 18, paragraph 2 first, and then punished jointly. Article 18: After the implementation of the Stamp Tax Law, all provisional stamp tax regulations, single-line rules of various provinces, and all precedents previously approved by the Ministry of Finance for exemption, delayed payment, or reduced stamp tax shall be abolished uniformly. Article 19: These implementation rules shall be implemented on the same day as the Stamp Tax Law.

Telegram from the General Chamber of Commerce

The National General Chamber of Commerce, in order to forward the Stamp Tax matters, sent a telegram to the national chambers of commerce, stating, "Recently, the Ministry of Finance Tax Tax No. 2660 Gray Daily telegram opened, (telegram text see above)" and attached a copy of the Stamp Tax Law and the implementation rules of the Stamp Tax Law to the meeting. In this regard, a copy is enclosed, and a telegram is sent to your association, hoping that you will check and notify the compliance. Attachment, National General Chamber of Commerce Chairman Lin Kang Hou Stamp.

The National Products Association and the Loan Association Discuss Loan Opinions; Credit Loans for Small Factories Should Be Lent as Much as Possible; The Loan Association Replied Yesterday with the Handling of the Loan 82

Yu Hede and others, the executive committee members of the Municipal Citizens' Promotion of National Products Association, recently compiled the opinions of the National Products Factory on various items of industrial and commercial loans and submitted them to the Industrial and Commercial Loan Review Committee for adoption. The Loan Association replied yesterday with the handling of small credit loans, saying that the association's main purpose is to effectively relieve small industrial and commercial businesses and stabilize the market situation, and that it will provide convenience to each applicant within the possible scope. The official letters exchanged between the two associations are as follows:

Original letter from the National Products Association

Director: In the state of the world's economic depression and weak social consumption, our national products industry bears the brunt and feels the pain of maintaining hardship and regulating deficits. The entire national products industry is in its infancy and is suddenly hit, and the trend is in danger. It is of great importance to the national economy and people's livelihood. The whole country is planning to relieve and treat the symptoms and root causes at the same time, to reverse the decline and achieve stability together. Our association is a group of national products factories, sharing the danger and having the will to relieve, but lacking the ability to implement. According to the opinions repeatedly stated by the member factories, (1) Collateral loans are based on capital and credit, and are suitable for the implementation of medium and large factories, but not for the operation of small factories. (2) Small factories have no previous dealings with the silver and money industries, and they are very eager for credit loans of three to five hundred yuan. They should be loaned as much as possible to implement relief, and the qualifications of the guarantor should be lenient. (3) Credit loans should strictly limit the factories that manufacture national products and the stores that sell national products to obtain loans, and prevent leaks. It is about the government's relief to factories and the revival of the national products industry. Please grant our request for investigation and handling. The national products industry relies heavily on it.

Reply from the Loan Association

Director: Received your association's public letter No. 5513, acknowledging the opinions of the National Products Factory on industrial and commercial loans. We have learned that our association follows the orders of the ministry and handles the review and loan of industrial and commercial credit loans, with the main purpose of effectively relieving small industrial and commercial businesses and stabilizing the market situation. Regarding the condition that loan manufacturers are limited to those who operate national products, it is regarded as the only principle. Recently, we approved the letter from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, which transferred the request from the Noodle Industry Association for the member stores to change the guarantee procedures, with three joint guarantees and the association's seal, to apply for a small loan of less than 100 yuan. Our association has approved the change at the seventh meeting and can approve the loan after requesting instructions from the Ministry of Finance. It is also found that it is difficult for loan applicants to find two reliable commercial firms to guarantee them in accordance with the ten principles for loans promulgated by the ministry. It has also been decided to recommend that the Ministry of Finance change it to one shop guarantee to show consideration for each case. All these measures coincide with your brilliant insights. Our association provides convenience to each applicant within the possible scope. This kind of service spirit should be seen by the society. We have approved the letter and replied accordingly, hoping that you will check it for our reference.

Ministry of Finance: Urging Repayment of Financial Public Bonds; Orders the Money Trade Supervision Committee to Notify All Firms 83

The Shen Shi News Agency reports that the Ministry of Finance previously allocated 25 million yuan in financial public bonds from the 24th year of the Republic to relieve the panic in the money trade industry. At that time, the Ministry of Finance also appointed Xu Kan, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Gu Gechu, Qin Runqing, and others to form a Money Trade Supervision Committee to manage the lending affairs. Various money shops submitted relatively reliable collateral, which, after being reviewed and approved by the Supervision Committee, allowed them to receive financial public bond notes. They then used these notes to borrow cash from major banks such as the Bank of China at 80% of the face value to meet their needs. The money trade crisis at that time was able to be smoothly overcome due to the maintenance provided by these 25 million yuan in financial public bonds. A Shen Shi News Agency reporter learned yesterday that the Ministry of Finance believes that the period for which these public bonds were lent to the money trade has exceeded two months, and that the Shanghai money market is gradually easing, with the "劃頭" (discount rate) reduced to "白," and financial conditions have returned to a state of calm. The previously allocated financial public bonds should be urged for repayment at the opportune moment so that the public bonds can be allocated for other purposes. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance recently ordered the Money Trade Supervision Committee to separately notify each shop to find ways to redeem the previous loans to bring the matter to a conclusion. Yesterday, it was also reported by the money trade side that various shops are currently trying to repay the loans borrowed from the Ministry of Finance in succession. However, although the current money trade is gradually turning around due to loans related to silk and tea, and the financial situation is indeed more advanced than several months ago, the general industrial and commercial situation has not yet fully improved. It is inevitable that there are still considerable difficulties in loaning and collecting accounts. It is difficult to fully repay the loans borrowed from the Ministry of Finance all at once. However, all firms are indeed separately raising funds to repay them to the best of their ability. Moreover, each shop has fully provided reliable collateral and considerable interest for this loan. If any shop has available cash to circulate, it is also willing to repay it as soon as possible to clear the formalities. The financial authorities are also very clear about all these circumstances.

Zhejiang Provincial Government Continues to Negotiate Autumn Cocoon Loan of 1 Million Yuan with Shanghai Banking Syndicate 84

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the banking syndicate composed of the Shanghai branches of the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, Zhejiang Xingye Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and the Fourteenth Bank established a spring cocoon loan of 1.8 million yuan on May 25. It was stipulated that if the amount of improved species of fresh cocoons collected exceeds 1.8 million yuan, the loan amount could be increased by up to 1.2 million yuan after consultation. Now, in view of the success of the loan and the significant relief obtained by the rural areas, and in accordance with the contract, repayments are being made successively. It is expected that the principal and interest will be fully repaid by January 24 of next year. The Zhejiang Provincial Government has now sent Chang Wei Xiang and Wu Shenbo of the Standing Committee of the Sericulture Improvement and Control Committee to negotiate with the banking syndicate composed of fourteen banks, including the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Zhejiang Xingye Bank, Shanghai Commercial Bank, Siming Bank, China Industrial Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Jin City Bank, Dalu Bank, Yanye Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, China National Products Bank, Tongshang Bank, and Kenye Bank, for a continuing autumn cocoon loan of 1 million yuan in national currency. The loan method will be modeled after the spring cocoon loan, with all the autumn cocoons collected and the silk reeled as collateral, interest calculated at 1% per month, and a term of eight months. It is said that success is largely expected.

The Dutch East Indies Still Discriminating Against Chinese; Recently Plans to Promulgate Import Tax on Chinese Goods to Restrict the Sale of Chinese Goods at Low Prices 88

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Dutch East Indies has been secretly discriminating against foreigners in recent years, especially against Chinese immigrants entering and leaving the islands, treating them more harshly than immigrants from Europe and the United States. Therefore, an import tax on Chinese immigrants was once promulgated to restrict the entry of Chinese immigrants. Later, after the Chinese Envoy to the Netherlands, Jin Wensi, was instructed by the government to argue with the Dutch authorities based on reason, demanding that the Dutch East Indies treat Filipino-Chinese immigrants equally with European and American immigrants in law, the matter subsided after repeated negotiations between the two sides. According to the news from the Chinese Expatriate Federation in this port, the Dutch East Indies recently plans to promulgate an import tax on Chinese goods. It is said that the purpose of setting this tax rate is to restrict Chinese goods from being sold at low prices in the Dutch East Indies. It is reported that the Chinese goods that have a considerable position in the Dutch East Indies market are tea, cotton cloth, and cosmetics.

Petition from the Rent Reduction Association in the Special District; Requesting the Party and Government to Clearly Define Rent Reduction Measures; Scheduled to Hold an Enlarged Petition 91

The Ren Gong News Agency reports that the First Special District Low Rent Committee, in order to request the government to clearly order rent reduction to stabilize society, resolved at its first executive committee meeting to send representatives to the party and government agencies on the 16th of this month to hold an enlarged petition, and decided to hold a rent reduction campaign week from the 25th to the 31st to attract attention. The association specially submitted petitions to the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Government, and the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, requesting the clear definition of rent reduction measures. The original petition stated that: "Submitting a petition for the purpose of stating the difficulties of the times and the hardship of the people, due to the depression in the market and the decline in commerce, and requesting the clear definition of rent reduction measures to maintain the situation. Since the end of the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, the social economy has been extremely panicked. The general public lives in fear and is on the verge of desperation. They run around and cry out, all hoping that the market will become more prosperous again. However, falling prices expose the weakness of people's purchasing power. Frequent lawsuits show the instability of social order. Thieves are rampant and take advantage of the situation. Starving people fill the streets in the thousands, and the situation is getting worse. The reason for this is all due to the social and economic panic. There are many ways to solve the social and economic problems. However, it has been found that the most severely exploited group among the current Shanghai citizens, and what often becomes the fatal blow to their livelihood and career, is the item of rent. The real estate industry in Shanghai is entirely speculative. A small amount of capital is used to obtain hundreds of times the profit, and it is resold repeatedly, accumulating interest. In the past, in a prosperous market, when industry and commerce were thriving and the social economy was active, it was still possible to exhaust the pond to catch the fish and drink poison to quench thirst. But now, with the depression in all industries and the depletion of the social economy, citizens who rent houses are really unable to continue to bear the high prices. Even if the welfare of the masses is not what those who operate real estate want to hear, high-rise buildings are closed one after another. People cannot live, and there is no one living in the houses. Regardless of whether this has an impact on individual economic relations or not, it affects society in a way that is great and huge. As a metropolis known as the Eastern civilization, how can we tolerate this phenomenon? Foreigners often criticize us as a society without order or organization, which they have seen and said. The Three People's Principles of the President of the Party place the greatest emphasis on the Principle of People's Livelihood, and the four needs of the Principle of People's Livelihood are listed and emphasized equally. Now, the citizens of Shanghai feel particularly pained by the housing problem, and the impact of this is likely to affect the whole body. The association is deeply saddened by this and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we submit this document and respectfully ask you to examine the plight of the citizens and quickly order a clear plan to reduce rents in order to maintain the situation and alleviate the hardship of the people. We are extremely grateful."

Fan Deran Talks About the Current Situation of the Hunan Paper Mill 97

Fan Deran, a paper-making expert and the current director of the Hunan Paper Mill, arrived in Shanghai from Hunan a few days ago. He has been visiting various paper mills in this port for days, purchasing materials, and attending banquets in various places, which has been very busy. He was originally scheduled to return to Hunan immediately to preside over the factory affairs. Now, due to physical discomfort, he intends to stay for a few more days. It is reported that he has sought medical treatment at the clinic of Dr. Huang Shaoshi, a Belgian medical doctor, using a shortwave diathermy apparatus to perform new-style electrotherapy and gradually recover his health. According to Fan, Hunan Province promoted machine paper-making, starting with the Huafeng Paper Mill in the first year of the Republic of China. The factory was originally a joint venture between the government and merchants. However, after the machine was installed, it failed repeatedly. Coupled with the impact of the political situation, it was suspended for more than 20 years. Many machine parts were lost, and those that remained were rusted. He (Fan said of himself) returned to Hunan from Paris and served in the Construction Department as a construction specialist. He was ordered to survey the factory. Seeing the dilapidated houses, he could not help but feel the desolation of the Hunan industry. After detailed investigation, he believed that although the factory's machines were incomplete and uneven, they could still be used if repaired. Rather than spending money and time to create a new factory, it was better to restore it on the existing foundation. After there was production performance, it could be expanded again. Therefore, he reported to the Construction Department, drafted a restoration plan, and submitted it to the Provincial Affairs Conference for approval. He reorganized the Hunan Paper Company, which was still a joint venture between the government and merchants. In July of last year, he started the machine test. At the same time, a cotton wadding factory was established near the yarn factory, using the factory's waste cotton as raw material. Products such as Mei Xuan, Tang Pinggong, and Material Half paper have been produced for printing stationery, envelopes, books, and forms. However, using waste cotton as raw material may have limited sources. In the future, as the quantity of products increases, there may be a shortage. Therefore, rice straw produced in Hunan was used as raw material, and kraft and newsprint papers have been produced. Its toughness is no less than that of imported products.

The Human-Powered Vehicle Association Special District Office issued a notice to the vehicle owners' introductions, the original text of which is: "For the purpose of notification, regarding the registration of rickshaw pullers in our special district, since it was heard that the Engineering Bureau had a deadline of July 31, after repeated written negotiations by this office, it was only allowed that if there are unregistered rickshaw pullers, they should be limited to bringing the vehicle to the original registration office for registration from August 1 to 15 to remedy the situation. Now, the deadline is not far away. We hope that each vehicle owner will step up the supervision of unregistered rickshaw pullers, send them to register as much as possible. It is necessary to know that this matter concerns the future of driving, the more the better, and do not miss the opportunity. Another item of testing and donation of new vehicles, the original plan was to test every two months, which has been changed to inspection once every four months. Later, due to poor vehicle repairs and unclean washing, the authorities believed that it affected the appearance of the city and informed that inspections should be carried out every two months. After serious negotiations by the representatives of this office, the result was that new vehicles, if they can be properly organized, will be allowed to be tested every four months, otherwise, the deadline for vehicle testing will still be handled according to the original intentions. The length of the deadline for vehicle testing depends on whether the vehicle owners can seriously organize it. The above two items are deeply related to the survival of the vehicle industry. At this time of business decline and the authorities' harsh demands, all our special district vehicle merchants must pay special attention and follow them diligently, and must not delay and make mistakes, which will lead to regrets in the future. This is a warning."

Public Announcement of the Simplified Life Insurance Regulations: The Savings & Remittance Bureau Budgets Opening Expenses, Actively Rushing Various Tasks for Implementation Next Month, Suggesting the Ministry of Education Compile a Simplified Life Insurance Textbook 106

The national simplified life insurance regulations have been publicly announced by the central government. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau has budgeted all the implementation expenses and has petitioned the Ministry of Transportation to request the Ministry of Education to include an insurance lesson in elementary school textbooks to instill insurance knowledge in the people. The details are as follows:

Regulations Announced: The simplified life insurance matter has been actively prepared by the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation. Drawing reference from state-run and private life insurance practices in England, America, and Japan, it drafted regulations comprising seventy-two articles, submitting them to the Ministry of Transportation, which then forwarded them to the Executive Yuan for review. The Executive Yuan revised and reduced them to seventy-one articles, which have been formally approved and promulgated. The Bureau's insurance division has completed the actuarial tables for mortality based on age, as well as examples of premium calculations. It is currently drafting various internal operational guidelines.

Budgeted Expenses: A reporter from the Da Gong She visited Zhang Mingting, the deputy director of the Insurance Division of the Savings and Remittance Bureau yesterday morning. When asked about the implementation time of simplified life insurance, he replied that although the regulations have been announced by the central government, the internal preparation procedures are quite complicated. The nature of simplified life insurance differs from ordinary private life insurance businesses. Currently, the total opening expenses are being budgeted. The Bureau hopes to implement it by mid-September, but it is still questionable whether all the procedures can be completed by then.

Insurance Textbook: Director Zhang also mentioned that various countries have achieved extraordinary development in the life insurance business. In Japan, simplified insurance has been incorporated into school textbooks to instill common knowledge in the public and promote their interest. The Bureau is also emulating this approach and has petitioned the Ministry of Transportation to request the Ministry of Education to add a simplified life insurance lesson to elementary school textbooks to promote awareness and increase knowledge. The Ministry of Transportation has shown great approval and has forwarded it to the Ministry of Education for adoption and implementation.

Zhabei Health Center: New Building Expected to be Completed in November 107

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, aiming to popularize health work in the urban area, originally planned to establish health centers in various districts to be responsible for local health, disease prevention, environmental sanitation, and other health-related work. However, due to the high cost, it could not be completed urgently. Therefore, it adopted a method of establishing them year by year. Districts such as Gaoqiao, Wusong, Jiangwan, and Hunan have been established successively from 1929 to 1934. However, the municipal government considers this administrative organization an essential task for protecting the people's health and decided to establish the Hubei District and Pudong District Health Centers in 1935, even in times of financial constraints. The Zhabei District Health Center, located on Qingyun Road, began construction in the middle of last month and is expected to be fully completed by the end of November this year. The budget for construction and equipment is limited to 50,000 yuan.

Heavy Rain in Shanghai This Morning: Water Accumulation in Low-Lying Areas, Rickshaw Pullers Enjoyed Threefold Profits 117

For the past month, Shanghai and its surrounding towns have experienced frequent heavy rains. From 8:00 AM this morning, Shanghai experienced another heavy rain, pouring down for about an hour before slowing slightly. However, light rain continued to fall until noon. After the heavy rain, the sky was dark, and lights were needed indoors. Water accumulated to a depth of one chi in low-lying areas of the city. Even the Sichuan Road and Wangping Street areas, which had been elevated, were submerged to the ankles. Water was even deeper in the area of the South Railway Station in Nanshi. Crossing streets relied entirely on rickshaw crossings, so rickshaw pullers enjoyed profits three times higher than usual. As for the current state of the fields, now is the time to spread fertilizer. After the heavy rain this morning, those who had already applied fertilizer were washed away, which is also a loss for farmers.

Fundraising Entertainment: Announcement to Compatriots

The association is holding a fundraising variety show for flood relief and has issued an announcement to all circles in Shanghai. Since the beginning of this summer, heavy rains have been rampant, and floods have caused disasters. The Yangtze River overflowed first, and the Yellow River breached its banks later. Other major tributaries were also in emergency situations simultaneously. The severity of the disasters is unprecedented. According to reports from various sources, the disaster area covers more than ten provinces, including Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Guangdong, Shandong, Henan, Hebei, and Shaanxi. Wherever the floodwaters reached, people and animals were swept away, and houses were destroyed. The number of people unfortunately buried in the bellies of fish is no less than hundreds of thousands, and the number of displaced victims is even more incalculable. Truly, wails of grief echo everywhere, and the sights are too tragic to bear and the sounds too unbearable to hear. Now that the hot summer has just passed and the cool autumn is coming, those poor victims are wandering with nowhere to go, without food when hungry and without clothing when cold. Farmland has been flooded, and houses are like ruins. The need for help is as urgent as a military fire. We, colleagues, mindful of the deep ties of kinship among compatriots, cannot bear to sit idly by. Hence, the Shanghai All-Circles Fundraising Variety Show for Flood Relief was initiated. Since the preparations began, we have been deeply grateful for the support from all circles and have been actively proceeding. We are now ready for the opening of the show and wish to share our thoughts with all our compatriots in Shanghai. Shanghai's cosmopolitan area stretches for ten miles, with bright lights and lavish spending in abundance. Although it has been affected by international monetary policies in recent years and financial difficulties are gradually emerging, judging by the crowded conditions in various entertainment venues and the congested entrances and exits of theaters, it is clear that our Shanghai compatriots are not completely incapable of saving the victims. Furthermore, the countryside is the foundation of the city. If the countryside goes bankrupt, the city will lose its foundation. Now, the vast countryside is under severe disaster and cannot recover. Raising funds for relief and promoting its restoration will directly save the victims and indirectly save ourselves. Only with the countryside can the prosperity of the city be summoned. Alas, compatriots, the national crisis is deep, and the disasters are severe. National subjugation and racial extinction are imminent. If we do not save ourselves, who will save us? The poorer the society and the more dangerous the country, the more we should demonstrate the spirit of mutual assistance and self-reliance among the Chinese people. Today's Chinese people, whether in the city or in the countryside, are about to fall into an unpredictable fate. Since their situations are the same, they should comfort each other and support each other. If we do not take this path, we will only accelerate the collapse and demise of our nation. The association's appeal to all circles is only to earnestly seek universal mobilization for fundraising, not to expect all Shanghai compatriots to come to the association to enjoy the variety show. However, those who enjoy the variety show are certainly welcome to come and support this righteous cause, as they can relieve their minds and bodies through entertainment and benefit the victims at the same time, truly achieving two good things with one action. This urgent plea is presented with the hope that it will be appreciated.

Ministry of Railways Orders Railway Bureaus to Change Kilograms to Market Jin: One Kilogram Converts to Two Market Jin 121

The two Railway Administration Bureaus received a telegram yesterday from the Ministry of Railways saying, "Regarding the 31st proposal of the 9th National Railway Transportation Conference, the Jinpu Railway proposed that 'all clauses in the Passenger Train Transportation Regulations that convert kilograms to Chinese Jin should be changed to convert to Market Jin for ease of calculation.' The proposal was passed by the general meeting and notified to all railways that 'the words 'Chinese Jin' should be changed to 'Market Jin' in all clauses of the Passenger Train Transportation Regulations.' However, the ratio of converting kilograms to Chinese Jin is different from that of converting kilograms to Market Jin. The previous number of kilograms converted to Chinese Jin in the clauses of the Passenger Transport Regulations should be revised to the number of Market Jin according to the ratio of kilograms converted to Market Jin (one kilogram converts to two Market Jin). Also, regarding the instruction No. 2539 revising clause 77 of the Passenger Transportation Regulations, the words '25 Market Jin' should be changed to '30 Market Jin.' In addition to the separate telegram, you are ordered to comply. Minister Gu Mengyu, Political Vice Minister Zeng Zhongming Acting, Yu Ye Yin. The Bureau has ordered the Traffic Department to comply.

Pinzhen Jewelry Store Suspected of Tax Evasion: Customs Requests Search, Confiscates Expensive Diamond Jewelry 123

Pinzhen Jewelry Store at 639 Nanjing Road is best known for its low-profit sales, leading to a not-bad business. However, the Jianghai Customs Service recently discovered that the goods sold by the store were suspected of tax evasion. It sent a letter to the Legal Department of the Public Works Bureau requesting assistance in investigating and banning the business. The department then requested the First Special District Court to issue search warrant No. 12. At 3:55 PM the day before yesterday, Chinese detective Liang Laisheng and Western patrol chief Deng Gen, together with representatives from the Customs Service, rushed to search the store. They confiscated 215 diamond rings, 23 diamond-set gemstone rings, 16 diamond-set sapphire rings, 13 pairs of diamond earrings, 6 pairs of gemstone earrings, 2 pairs of black gemstone earrings, 11 gemstone brooches, 14 gemstone bracelets, 8 bracelets, 4 sapphire bracelets (all of the above are inlaid with diamonds), 15 bags of small loose diamonds, totaling 1,643 diamonds, and 11 account books, with a total value of 60,000 to 70,000 yuan. At the time, the items were placed in a leather suitcase, and Pinzhen manager Dong Shuyu, Western patrol chief Deng Gen, and Customs Service representative Pu Si each signed and sealed the box before taking it back to the Laozha police station. Yesterday morning, the items were sent to the Second Criminal Division of the First Special Court. Police station lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that, according to the Customs Service's report, Pinzhen Jewelry Store was suspected of violating Article 21 of the Anti-Smuggling Regulations. Therefore, the police station requested a search warrant from the court to conduct the search. At the time, the store manager could not provide invoices or other proof of purchase. It is now requested that the confiscated items be temporarily detained at the police station, while the 11 account books be handed over to the Customs Service personnel for investigation. Customs Service representative Pu Si testified that the diamonds sold by Pinzhen did not match the Customs Service's records, so they were considered to be suspected of tax evasion. Pinzhen manager Dong Shuyu stated that the diamonds purchased by the store were mostly traded in cash on the market according to industry practice and did not have invoices, and were not purchased from overseas. He also hired lawyer Fan Gang to appear in court and requested that the Customs Service provide sufficient evidence to prove that Pinzhen's goods were tax-evaded. After Magistrate Zhan Liangce reported the matter, it was ordered that the confiscated items be detained until next Tuesday for further review, and the 11 account books be handed over to the Customs Service personnel for immediate investigation.
