Garment Makers' Guild: Water Festival Leads to Disaster; Steamboat Collides with Festival Boat; Wang Amao Tragically Perishes 127

The local Shanghai North City garment makers' guild recently collected funds to hold a water and land Taoist ceremony for three days. The day before yesterday (the 11th) was the last day. They hired a Xin Zhen Chang steamboat to tow two pier boats behind (the two boats were side by side). The boats were fully loaded with ingots, paper clothes, a large number, and carried six monks chanting Buddhist scriptures. The sound of drums and gongs was deafening, and many members of the guild were on the boats burning ingots and paper clothes, all extremely excited. Unexpectedly, joy turned to sorrow. The Xin Zhen Chang steamboat was sailing from south to north. Near Yangshupu, a Zhang Jia Bang (boat name) steamboat was sailing from Pudong to Puxi. Because it was too late to avoid the collision, it violently crashed into the pier boat being towed by Xin Zhen Chang. Wang Amao (20 years old, local resident of Huade Road), a garment maker squatting at the bow of the boat burning paper money, and two others were knocked into the river. Two people were rescued immediately, but Wang Amao had already joined the water ghosts, with no trace of his body. This greatly dampened the spirits and led to a dispirited end to the celebration. It was not until 7 a.m. yesterday that the water police patrol boat finally recovered Wang Amao's body, taking it to the Lifesaving Bureau at the South Wharf. The patrol head sent detectives Yao Guofa and Xu Juelu to inform the deceased's father, Wang Jinsheng, to apply to the local court for an autopsy. After an interrogation by Inspector Zhao Chuanjia, he went to the Lifesaving Bureau on the Bund to verify the cause of death. Observers said the deceased's father hastily prepared a coffin to await further instructions.

Pingxin Steamboat Capsizes Rowboat: Drowning Incident; Passengers Suffer Great Losses; Steamboat Captain Detained for Investigation 128

The Pingxin steamboat of the Hu Nan-Min Nan Company, which travels to and from Pinghu and other places, is docked at the Guan Dock in Nanshi. On the afternoon of the 11th of this month, at 6:30 PM, the steamboat returned from Pinghu to Shanghai. While passing the Jianghai Customs South Checkpoint (near the Shenjia Garden, known as the Yucheng Foreign Customs), it stopped the engine for customs inspection as usual. Passengers Huang Zhuqi, Huang Xiangzhao, Xu Yougen, Fu Tingzhang, and two others intended to disembark at the pier nearby. They hired a rowboat operated by the Shandong siblings Sun Shannv (21 years old) and Sun Xiaoyatou (16 years old) to ferry them ashore. Sun Shannv and her sister tied the rowboat to the steamboat. Sun Shannv was at the stern of the rowboat holding onto the steamboat's iron bar, while Sun Xiaoyatou was at the bow of the rowboat holding onto the steamboat, so that passengers could cross. Huang Zhuqi and the others had already crossed to the rowboat and Fu Tingzhang was in the process of crossing when the steamboat unexpectedly rang the bell and started to move. So, Fu retreated back to the steamboat. At that time, the tide was rapid, and as the steamboat turned, the rowboat could not withstand the force and immediately capsized. Everyone on board fell into the water. Except for the passengers Huang Zhuqi and the other four, and Sun Xiaoyatou, who were rescued on the spot, Sun Shannv was drowned. The water police arrested the steamboat captain, Wang Ahai (51 years old, from Changshu), who caused the accident, and detained him in the police station. Sun Shannv's body was recovered from the river at the South Wharf at 2:45 PM the day before yesterday (the 12th) and taken to the Lifesaving Bureau to await an autopsy. Yesterday morning, the water police summoned witnesses Huang Zhuqi, Huang Xiangzhao, Xu Yougen, and the deceased's father, Sun Xiaomao (52 years old, from Shandong, who usually relied on his children to operate the boat for a living), for questioning. They prepared a document and sent detective Cheng Yongnian to escort Wang Ahai, the captain of the Min Nan steamboat, who was suspected of negligence, and the witnesses to the local court for interrogation and to request an autopsy. After being interrogated by Inspector Zhao Chuanjia, he ordered Wang Ahai to be detained. He then led Inspector Xuan Zhiming to the Lifesaving Bureau on the Bund, where they verified that Sun Shannv had indeed drowned. A report was filled out instructing the deceased's father, Sun Xiaomao, to prepare a coffin and await further instructions. It is reported that the luggage and baskets carried by the five passengers who fell into the water were all washed away, resulting in a total loss of over a thousand taels of silver.

Feud Over Money: Good Friends Turn on Each Other; Feng Muqing Chopped but Not Lightly Wounded; Qian Shanhai Suddenly Changes His Testimony 129

Qian Shanhai, 28 years old, from Longhua in the western suburbs of this county, and Feng Muqing, 30 years old, a local resident living at No. 130, Liu Jia Nong, Maiqi Road, Rue de Brenas, French Concession, both swore allegiance to the renowned gangster brothers, Mr. Gu, as their "old man." Therefore, Qian and Feng were nominally sworn brothers. Previously, they jointly invested capital to manufacture fake banknotes, which Feng embezzled, leading to a deep-seated feud. Unable to vent his anger, Qian gathered Zhou Fugeng, Wang Laoer, Afu, Xuan Gen, and five or six others who are currently at large at around 6 a.m. on June 18th of this year. Armed with axes, they rushed to Feng's home. When the servant woman opened the door to take out the chamber pot, Qian and the others rushed inside and into Feng's bedroom. At that time, Feng was still fast asleep in bed. Qian and the others, without asking any questions, dragged Feng out of bed and chopped at his legs with thirteen axe blows, leaving behind a threatening letter (saying that this attack was just a warning, and that if they reported it to the police, they would surely be killed). Afterwards, Feng did not report to the police but went to the Red Cross General Hospital for treatment. Time passed, but on the 14th of last month, Feng received another threatening letter in the hospital. The hospital reported it to the police, and detective Zhi Zhenglong went to the hospital to investigate Feng's past injuries. On the morning of the 2nd of this month, at around 1 a.m., the detectives learned that the suspect Qian Shanhai was hiding in Room 12 of the Hai Dong Chun Hotel, No. 15, Yunnan Road, Public Concession. They, along with the Old Zha Police Station, sent detectives to arrest Qian. The next day, he was sent to the Special Second Court. During the interrogation, Qian confessed that because Feng had been harsh and humiliating, he had gathered people to attack him. The court ordered him to be detained and scheduled another hearing. This was reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning at 11 a.m., Judge Zhang Chaozuo of the Special Second Court continued the hearing in the Criminal Division One. Lawyer Yuan Yu of the Police Department stated the results of the police investigation and filed charges of intentional injury under Article 277, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. The victim, Feng Muqing, then testified about the circumstances of the attack, saying that he and the defendant had been friends but had a grudge over money dating back three or four years. When asked, the defendant Qian Shanhai denied his previous testimony, adamantly denying that he had gone to attack the plaintiff and denying any previous difficulties with the plaintiff. The court repeatedly challenged him, but the defendant vehemently protested his innocence and hired lawyers Fan Gang and Fan Shisheng to appear in court to defend him. The court ordered the victim to go to the forensic medical examination for his injuries and ordered that arguments be made. The court then declared the hearing closed and scheduled sentencing. The defendant was returned to custody.

Husband and Wife Cannot Sue Each Other: Wife Drags Husband to Police Station; Accuses Him of Obstructing Freedom and Abandonment; Hopes the Police Station Will File a Public Prosecution 130

Xie Zhenxuan, 26 years old, from Zhenhai, who previously worked at the Ximen branch of the Shanghai Bank and currently resides at No. 226, London Road, Xibao Xing Road, Zhabei, married Chen Yueying (22 years old), also from Zhenhai. Recently, due to disagreements, their relationship deteriorated. Chen Yueying hired a lawyer and filed a complaint with the Criminal Division of the Special Second Court, accusing her husband, Xie Zhenxuan, of obstructing her freedom and coercing her to sign a divorce agreement. She claimed that they had been married for six or seven years and that since returning to their hometown four months ago on February 17th, he had not provided her with a single penny for living expenses. Therefore, she came to Shanghai to reason with him. She first stayed at her aunt's house and then rented a place at No. 49, Qing An Lane, Tang Jia Wan. On June 9th, at 6 p.m., the defendant suddenly called me to the upper floor of the Shanghai Bank Ximen branch and forced me to sign a separation agreement. When I returned home and had someone read it, it turned out to be a divorce agreement. She immediately hired a lawyer to negotiate for the return of the agreement, but the defendant ignored her. She requested an investigation. First, Judge Sun Pengxian of the Special Second Court opened a hearing and summoned the parties. Because of jurisdictional errors, it was ruled to be transferred to the local court for trial. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiong Huiping of the Special Second Court opened a hearing in Criminal Division Two and summoned both parties and their lawyers. The plaintiff, Chen Yueying, first testified about how she was forced by her husband to sign the divorce agreement. The defendant, Xie Zhenxuan, testified that he was ill and, on the advice of his doctor, signed a separation agreement with his wife, not a divorce agreement. He stated that all the documents were in the plaintiff's possession. After reviewing the testimony, the court stated that since the parties were still formally married and not divorced, it was ruled that, according to Article 326 of the Criminal Procedure Law, husband and wife could not sue each other. The plaintiff should file a complaint with the police station. After the ruling, the court adjourned. After exiting the courtroom, the plaintiff, Chen Yueying, waited outside the court for the defendant, Xie Zhenxuan, to leave with his lawyer. She then grabbed Xie and took him to the French police station next to the court to request an investigation. In addition to the obstruction of freedom alleged in the complaint, she also added a charge of abandonment.

Debt Due to Marriage of Children: Unable to Make Ends Meet, Commits Suicide; Xu Zhihui, So Pitiful 131

Xu Zhihui, 51 years old, from Ningbo, residing at No. 9, Da An Fang, No. 182, Pu En Ji Shi Road, French Concession, had been working as an accountant at Gong Mao Wildlife Shop, Nos. 18 and 20, Caishi Street, for many years. In recent years, he had accumulated debts of thousands of taels of silver due to the marriage of his children. Recently, due to urgent demands from creditors, he was unable to make ends meet, leading him to take his own life. On the afternoon of the 12th, he returned home from the shop at 4 p.m. After having dinner at 6 p.m., he went to bed at 8 p.m. At 2 a.m., he got up while his wife, children, and daughters-in-law were asleep and swallowed Lysol disinfectant to commit suicide. He groaned incessantly after poisoning himself. His wife, Ms. Hu, discovered this when she noticed an empty bottle of Lysol on the table in front of the bed. She immediately hired a car to take him to Guangci Hospital. However, the poisoning was too severe, and treatment was ineffective. He died about half an hour after being admitted to the hospital, at 3 a.m. The hospital reported the incident to the Zhaojiawan Central Police Station as per regulations. Detectives were sent to investigate the cause of the suicide. The body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch morgue for an autopsy. Yesterday morning, the police summoned the deceased's wife, Xu Hu, and Xu Zhongxing, to the police station. They reported to the Special Second Court and requested Inspector Wang Ren to come to the morgue with forensic doctor Wei and clerk Peng Shujiguan at noon. They confirmed that Xu Zhihui had died by poisoning himself before death. After taking his seat, detective Zhang Chunsheng reported on the investigation. The officer questioned the deceased's wife. He then ordered the body to be released to the family for burial after they had signed a guarantee.

Tang Guoshu: Tragic Suicide by Jumping from Building 132

Tang Guoshu, about 20 years old, from Guangdong, lived at No. 75, Yong Ji Lane, Laobazi Road, Hongkou. Yesterday afternoon at around 4 p.m., Tang Guoshu, for unknown reasons, suddenly went to the third floor of a building at No. 1280, North Sichuan Road, and committed suicide by jumping from the building. He fell onto the sidewalk, his brains splattered, and blood flowed profusely. He was unconscious. Afterwards, Chinese Constable No. 539 discovered him. Before he could be treated, he died. His body was transferred to the morgue to await an autopsy.

Patrol Police: Seize Large Quantity of Red Pills; Three Suspects Arrested 133

Yesterday (the 13th) afternoon at around 3 p.m., one hour before the departure of the 302nd Shanghai-Ping train on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway at the North Shanghai Station, as passengers were boarding the train, Zhang Baoren, the section chief of the railway police section, and detective Chen Rongnian, were patrolling the platform. They saw three or four passengers carrying hand luggage hurriedly boarding the train, acting suspiciously. Zhang and Chen immediately followed them onto the train. When questioning them, they were evasive. The three passengers and a rattan bag, two small leather bags were detained. They were taken to the office of the 3rd Railway Police Division. Upon opening them in public, there were seventeen biscuit tins containing 340,000 red pills, weighing 37 kilograms in total. Three third-class tickets to Nanjing and one third-class ticket to Xuzhou were also found on the suspects. According to their confession, Wen Younian, 39 years old, from Luoyang, Henan; Wu Delin, 42 years old, from Luoyang, Henan; and Wang Jintang, 21 years old, from Xin'an, Henan. Another person had already escaped upon hearing the news. They had all mixed in through the east and west gates of the North Station yesterday afternoon, intending to sell them in other places. The railway police section is currently pursuing the fugitive in order to bring him to justice.

Three Years of Injustice: Hu Xuan Ting and Wife's Retrial Declared Not Guilty 134

Hu Xuan Ting, 47, a Cantonese man, formerly worked for the China Motor Company, and lived with his wife, Hu Liao, 28, at 30 Jiaotong Lane, Qiujiang Road, Shanghai. On the evening of October 25, 1932, Jiang Mao, who lived with the couple, was ill in bed. As her four-year-old daughter, Xiaozhuzi, lacked care, she asked Hu Liao to stay with the child. Hu Xuan Ting returned home from work around 11 pm that night. When he saw the little girl in bed, he asked about the situation and instructed his wife to cover her well and keep her from catching a cold, before going to bed. The next morning, Xiaozhuzi got up and went home. The following day, Jiang Mao saw that Xiaozhuzi was urinating blood. Suspecting that Hu Xuan Ting had raped the girl, she accused Hu Xuan Ting of raping a young girl and Hu Liao of assisting in the rape at the Shanghai District Court. Several days later, Xiaozhuzi died from her illness. Jiang Mao then accused the Hu couple of raping the girl and causing her death. In the first trial, Hu Xuan Ting was sentenced to life imprisonment, and Hu Liao was sentenced to 13 years' imprisonment. The Hu couple appealed to the High Court, which overturned the verdict and declared them innocent. The prosecutor appealed to the Supreme Court, which ordered a retrial. Hu was still convicted according to the first trial, while Hu Liao's sentence was reduced to 12 years. The Hu couple again appealed to the Supreme Court. In May of this year, another retrial was ordered. The Guangdong compatriots in Shanghai felt injustice and jointly requested the Guangdong Shanghai Association to provide legal assistance. The Association, considering that the case involved a fellow townsman being falsely accused, appointed Guo Qiming, a lawyer and director of the Association, to go to Jiangsu to provide pro bono defense. The case was announced on the 2nd of this month, and the Hu couple were found not guilty. The three years of injustice have finally been redressed. The couple have praised the virtue of lawyer Guo Qiiming.

Two Women Attempt Suicide with Poison: One Dead... One May Be Saved 137

Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, a fashionable woman, wearing a white Indian silk cheongsam and high-heeled leather shoes, in her early twenties and speaking with a Cantonese accent, came to the Renji Hotel on North Sichuan Road. She claimed to be surnamed Feng and requested a room. The bellboy checked her in and led her to the second floor. After inspecting a room, she did not make a decision and left. Around 6:00 PM, the woman returned with another woman carrying a small rattan basket. They rented room number 69. The woman identified herself as Feng Baozhen, a Cantonese native, aged 18. The other woman's name was not given. They retired for the night. The next day at noon, the tea attendant, following regulations, knocked on the door to inquire if they needed anything. After a long period of no response, he managed to force the door open. He found the two women lying unconscious on the bed, their faces ashen. Suspecting poisoning, he immediately reported to the front desk, who in turn notified the police and called an ambulance to rush them to the Shanghai Sanitarium on Bazilu (靶子路). One of the women, identified as Feng Baozhen, regained consciousness after receiving an injection from the doctor, and her life may be saved. The other woman, however, had taken too much poison and could not be revived. She died shortly after. The police station on Minxing Road is currently investigating the identities of the two women and the reason for their suicide attempt.

Sending Bigu Pills to Disaster Areas for Relief

Zhao Daozhang of the Daozi Relief Association in this city received a telegram from the Daozi Relief Association in Jining, Shandong, stating that the area had suffered severe flooding this summer, and the famine victims were desperately in need of food. Zhao Daozhang personally went to Xu Chongdao Pharmacy on Avenue Edward VII (愛文義路) a few days ago and ordered the first batch of over 1,000 catties (斤) of hunger-relief Bigu Xian Dan (辟穀仙丹), totaling more than 50,000 pills, packed into fifteen large boxes. On the afternoon of the 13th, the China Travel Service shipped them to Jining to Officer Wang (王長官) for distribution to the disaster areas. More are being made and will be shipped soon. It is said that taking one pill a day can stave off hunger for a day. This is better than other foods for famine victims who are extremely hungry. For famine victims who lack rice and wheat, taking these pills can replace the function of rice and wheat. Furthermore, the price is extremely low, making it easy to distribute widely.

The Reorganization Office Begins Re-registration

After the Special Party Department of the Jin-Hu, Hu-Hang-Yong Railway (京滬滬杭甬鐵路) reassigned some instructors and reorganizers, the current instructors Zhang Yunhe (張雲鶴) and Wang Shouheng (王守恒), and reorganizers Yuan Qiaofu (袁巧福), Hong Desheng (洪德生), Tang Ziliang (唐子良), Cai Wanquan (蔡萬泉), and Yao Xiaojiang (姚筱江), recently received instructions from the Special Party Department of the Jin-Hu, Hu-Hang-Yong Railway, which in turn were instructions from the Central People's Movement Committee. Because the previous membership registration had some omissions, a remedial measure was issued. The office has already drafted a re-registration and re-election method and notified all railway workers, setting the period from now until the 24th of this month for re-registration and re-election, so that the reorganization work can be completed before the end of this month and a representative assembly can be convened as soon as possible. The original text of the notice is attached below for your information.

Notice: It has been found that the Executive Committee of the Special Party Department of the Jin-Hu, Hu-Hang-Yong Railway of the Chinese Kuomintang issued instruction Zhi Zi (職字) No. 152, which briefly stated: "The Central People's Movement Guidance Committee issued instruction No. 10398, which briefly stated: "After this committee sent personnel to reorganize the union, and after this committee sent personnel to inspect, it was believed that the union reorganization work on this railway was proceeding purely in accordance with legal procedures in terms of planning. However, in the process of implementation, there were some careless aspects. For example, there were many real workers at each station who had not been registered. It seemed that appropriate remedies should be given." Remedies were drafted and submitted to the committee. The remedial measures were found to be feasible. In addition to a letter to the Ministry of Railways, we have copied one piece of the remedial measure and ordered you to comply with it." Upon receiving this order, we copied and issued the relevant measures and ordered you to comply with them. Upon receiving this order, we checked and found that more than 8,600 members of our office have already been registered in accordance with the law. Unfortunately, a small number of members had a wait-and-see attitude during the last registration and did not register. Now, in compliance with the order, we will carry out a supplementary registration, setting the period from now until the 24th of this month for the supplementary registration. All workers in the car, machine, and engineering sections of this railway who have not yet registered must go to register in accordance with the following supplementary registration and re-election methods and participate in the election. Do not delay. In addition to separately notifying everyone, this is a notice for your information.

Supplementary Registration and Re-election Methods

1. Workers in the car, machine, and engineering sections who have not been registered may directly request registration from the local branch or sub-branch within the above-mentioned time limit.

2. This office will send personnel to join the sub-branch officers to distribute to the stations and sections that have not yet been registered, guiding the registration.

3. Members who are registered in the supplementary registration will still be appropriately divided into groups according to the nature of their work and the work environment.

4. If the number of people registered in a supplementary registration in each group exceeds two-thirds of the original number of people, the group should be re-elected.

5. If more than two-thirds of the groups belonging to each branch are re-elected, the branch should also be re-elected. The same applies if each sub-branch has the same situation.

6. Members registered in the supplementary registration may separately schedule an election of representatives according to the original regulations on the number of people in the representative assembly election groups of the entire railway.

Instructors Zhang Yunhe, Wang Shouheng, Zhang Xiangfa; Reorganizers Yuan Qiaofu, Hong Desheng, Cai Wanquan, Tang Ziliang, Yao Xiaojiang, August 12, 1935.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 243rd Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Convertible Notes states: "In accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the amount of convertible notes issued by this bank and the reserve funds. We held the 243rd inspection at the Issuing Bureau of this bank on August 10, 1935, and hereby report the results of the inspection as follows:

(A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 10,795,833 silver dollars, including 10,104,2743 silver dollar notes and 6,915,570 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note reserve funds is 10,795,833 silver dollars, including 82,378,313 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve is kept in the issuing vault of this bank at 78,217,849 yuan, in branch banks in various ports at 2,289,216 yuan, and in other banks at 2,861,248 yuan. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 24,580,000 silver dollars.

(B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 373,324.7 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserve funds is 373,324.7 yuan. This reserve fund includes 7,351 taels, 9 mace and 5 fen of silver, which at the fixed price of .50779 amounts to 371,324.7 customs gold.

According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve should be at least 60%, and the rest should be guaranteed by legal guarantees. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby made.

August 12, 1935.

Li Fusun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank. Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yan Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiying.

Meeting Minutes of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association: Registered and Licensed Rickshaw Pullers are all Insured. Old Age Pension Fund for the Unemployed to be Sent Back to Their Hometowns.

The Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association convened a board of directors meeting last Friday, the 5th. Those present included Messi (Chairman), Peng Jin, Yin Zhiling, Chou Zitong, Zhu Luanheng, Tao Deman, Wang Zhiren, and others. Xie Dao'an and Gu Songmao were absent. Mr. Xie had sent a special letter requesting leave, expressing his apologies. At the meeting, a statistical report on the work of the Mutual Aid Association in July was submitted for discussion. It was generally felt that the progress of the association's affairs was smooth. The establishment of three new offices (in Nanshi, the French Concession, and Zhabei) was also a very satisfactory start. The association also received the following donations from major businesses: 7,000 paper fans from Dunlop Rubber Company, one set of a six-tube long and short wave radio from the China and West Drug Store, two sets of four-tube long and short wave radios from the Dahua Steel Factory, and 29 packages of medicine from Maoli Western Drug Store. The association has sent special letters of thanks to the above-mentioned businesses. The Special Relief Committee for Rickshaw Pullers Who Have Not Registered and Received Licenses recently held a meeting. At that time, because the scope of the problem had not been determined, it was difficult to determine the procedures to be followed. Therefore, it was decided to convene another meeting in late this month to present a report. In addition, the minutes of the two meetings of the Personnel Committee on the 24th and 30th of last month were also submitted to the Board of Directors for reporting. Apart from slight additions and deletions, they were generally agreed upon and passed. In addition, the Board of Directors also accepted the minutes of the two meetings of the Insurance Committee on the 22nd of last month and the 2nd of this month. The Board of Directors had a detailed discussion on insurance matters. As a result, the following resolutions were passed: (1) All rickshaw pullers who have been registered and licensed will be insured by the Mutual Aid Association, so that they will receive an indemnity of 40 yuan in the event of death or serious accidents. (2) 40,000 yuan will be allocated from the existing funds for the exclusive payment of insurance premiums. In addition, it was decided that if there is a surplus in the above-mentioned insurance plan at the end of the fiscal year, the surplus should be immediately withdrawn and allocated to the rickshaw puller old-age pension fund. The method of handling this subsidy will be determined in the future, but its general intention is to provide a certain amount of donation to rickshaw pullers who, due to old age, disability or other reasons, are unable to work, and to those who have paid mutual assistance fees for a certain period of time, but are unable to continue to enjoy mutual assistance rights due to the cessation of their occupation. The Board of Directors decided to first allocate 10,000 yuan from the funds at the discretion of the Custody Committee as the fundamental fund for old-age pensions. The Board of Directors also decided to request the Custody Committee to allocate 50,000 yuan from the accumulated mutual assistance fees to be used for the relief of unemployed rickshaw pullers and to assist them in returning to their hometowns. All rickshaw pullers who previously worked in the Public Concession but were not registered and licensed, and who were unable to pull rickshaws due to the limitation of the number of people or other reasons, so that they could not register and receive licenses, and were therefore unemployed, may be assisted by the Mutual Aid Association to return to their hometowns or given other relief. Furthermore, at the end of the meeting discussion, the Chairman mentioned that someone was distributing leaflets among the rickshaw pullers that day. The leaflets claimed to be issued by the Mutual Aid Association, but this was not the case. The leaflets stated that the Mutual Aid Association allowed the distribution of a large amount of food, clothing, money, etc., all of which were wishful thinking and unfounded. Their intention was nothing more than to instigate the rickshaw pullers to come to the association to make wanton demands, thereby damaging the reputation of the Mutual Aid Association. The Board of Directors of the Mutual Aid Association unanimously resolved that the means were despicable, and immediately decided to investigate and punish the person who made and distributed the leaflets.

Weather Report 139

The weather forecast from Xujiahui Observatory at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The area around Shandong is cloudy, but still sunny and clear, with fog and varying winds from the southeast to southwest. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River are clear and quite hot, with light and undirected winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River and the East China Sea have unstable winds and thunderstorms. American Wildlife Filmmaker Captures Extremely Valuable Wildlife Footage After Staying in India and Malaysia for a Long Time, He Discovered the Lifestyle of Savage Tribes 140

The North China Daily News reports that Mr. Booker, a famous American hunter and wildlife filmmaker, arrived in Shanghai last Saturday night on the mail ship "Nalder". At dawn on Tuesday, he had already departed for New York on the President Coolidge. Mr. Booker spent six months making another wildlife and forest film. He set out from New York on December 7 last year, travelling through Europe to India. He stayed in India for two months and shot several excellent tiger films. He then went to Malaysia and established a public office in Johor, where he received favorable treatment from the local sultan, who provided him with all kinds of assistance. In total, he shot 95,000 feet of film, but only 8,000 feet will be selected for use. The tentative name of the new film is "Fangs". Mr. Booker is now rushing back to the United States to spend two months editing the film and adding scenery and sound. One of the features of the film is the lifestyle of a savage tribe called the Sakais, who live deep in the forests of Malaysia. They are of medium height and originally occupied southern Asia. Today, they are declining and there are not many left. They know nothing about any of the tools of the new era. They still use stone for knives and axes, and their weapons are blowpipes and darts. Their lives are almost like those of wild animals, and they have not yet emerged from the primitive era. However, they are afraid of seeing outsiders. Mr. Booker spent a lot of time approaching them and finally gained their trust, allowing him to live in several villages for some time. Mr. Booker visited Shanghai six years ago. He was very surprised to see the great changes in the city's appearance this time. Mr. Booker may return to the Far East next year, and he still plans to visit Shanghai at that time.

Sports News

The Weather is Uncooperative, Heavy Rain Pours Down, Charity Tennis Match Rescheduled for Today, Starting at 3:30 PM Still at Singapore Road, Exhibition at Rong Garden Cancelled, Attempting to Retain Xu for a Few Days, Xu Won Four Games in a Row Against Lin Baohua Yesterday 141

The charity tennis tournament, originally scheduled to begin at 4:00 PM yesterday at the China Tennis Club on Singapore Road, had already experienced heavy rain yesterday morning. It stopped slightly at noon, so the audience went to Singapore Road continuously, with an estimated number of four or five hundred people. However, the weather was uncooperative. When the competition was about to begin, the rain suddenly intensified, followed by a downpour. Although the singles match between Xu Chengji (許承基) and Lin Baohua (林寶華) began in the rain, Xu Chengji won four games in a row. It was not possible to continue the match, and it was forced to stop. It was decided to postpone it to today, starting at 3:30 PM, still at the China Tennis Club. Tickets of five yuan and three yuan are still valid. Those present yesterday included Mayor Wu's representative Tang Shixuan (唐士煊), initiators Director Wu Xingya (吳醒亞) and his wife, Education Director Pan Gongzhan, Legislator Wu Kaixian (吳開先), and German Consul Kliber (克利伯) stationed in Shanghai. When the rain first came, the audience still stood in the rain, unwilling to leave. It was not until the match was stopped that they dispersed.

Xu Chengji is Unstoppable

Xu and Lin started the match in the rain. Lin served first, but Xu won the first game with a score of "slip four" (滑四). Then, when Xu served, Lin only managed to win one point. Xu's serves and corner shots left Lin Baohua at a loss and with no way to defend himself. Thus, in one breath, Xu Chengji won four games in a row, taking a 4-0 lead. The match lasted less than ten minutes. At this point, due to the heavy rain, the match was announced to be stopped. Xu and Lin will continue the match this afternoon. The schedule is as follows:

(1) Xu Chengji vs. Lin Baohua, starting at 3:30 PM, singles (Xu leads 4-0)

(2) Qiu Feihai (邱飛海) vs. Carlson, 4:15 PM, singles

(3) Xu Chengji and Lin Baohua vs. Carlson and Defu (德孚), 5:00 PM, doubles

Trying to Retain Xu Chengji

Xu was originally scheduled to perform at Rong Garden today, but it had to be cancelled due to the postponement of the charity event. Xu is scheduled to leave Shanghai tomorrow to return south, so Chen Qihao (陳其浩), Tan Jing (潭敬), and other enthusiastic tennis fans are discussing with Xu to stay in Shanghai for a few more days. If Mr. Xu's schedule is a concern, they plan to send Mr. Xu to Hong Kong by plane and then take a boat to Singapore. Mr. Xu has indicated his willingness to agree. If it does not rain again, there may be an opportunity to perform at Rong Garden.

Tianjin's 35th Army Polo Team Will Have Difficulty Coming to Shanghai Temporarily Due to Problems with Horses 147

Xiamen YMCA: The 5th Annual Gulangyu-Xiamen Cross-Harbor Swimming Competition - Chen Shulin of Jimei Wins First Place 151

(Xiamen Correspondence) The Xiamen YMCA held its 5th Annual Gulangyu-Xiamen Cross-Harbor Swimming Competition on August 3rd. That morning, General Secretary of the YMCA, Shen Zhizhong, and Sports Secretary, Lu Dalun, arrived at the starting and ending points between Gulangyu and Xiamen to survey and prepare everything. After 2 PM, spectators lined both shores, with an especially large number of boats on the water, totaling no less than three thousand people. The Water Police First Brigade and the Public Security Third Bureau were responsible for water and land traffic control. The directors, staff, and officers of the YMCA, including Zhang Shixiong, Ma Zongse, Ding Yuehan (Inspection Division), Yang Xubao, Du Shenyuan (Timing Division), Zhuang Jifu, Lin Xiuwu, Lin Zongjing, Zhuang Yagu (Record Division), Rong Zihua, Wen Yao (Finish Line Judging Division), Ke Fuliang, Du Zunen (Rescue Division), and Zhang Yuantong (Photography Division), arrived at the venue one after another. At 2:15 PM, the starter, Lu Dalun, called the roll, and seventy-six people reported. Due to the rising tide, the start was moved up to 2:40 PM. At the sound of the starter's gun, seventy-five male and female athletes entered the water. Because there were too many spectator boats, some difficulties arose in traffic control. Fortunately, the water police patrol boats maintained order effectively, and the competitors were able to pass smoothly and reach the finish line. Chen Shulin of Jimei won the championship with a time of ten minutes and forty-eight seconds amidst cheers. (Wang Honglong had won the third and fourth competitions; his fourth competition record was ten minutes, eight seconds, and seven-tenths of a second). A total of sixty-one people finished after him (fifty-one men, forty-one finished; six women, five finished; nineteen children, fifteen finished). Because the waves were extremely strong, some drifted to the Xiamen Port area. These were guided and escorted ashore by the YMCA authorities and the water police patrol boats. Although the results were approximately forty seconds slower than last year due to the post-typhoon conditions and strong waves, public opinion was highly satisfied with these results considering the water's resistance. The names of the winners are listed below:

(Men's Division) Champion: Chen Shulin (time: ten minutes and forty-eight seconds), (2) Fu Zonglin, (3) Lin Huitian, (4) Hong Anxun, (5) Cai Lianlu, (6) Wang Honglong (last year's champion), (7) Zhang Hongsheng, (8) Guo Jie.

(Women's Division) Champion: Han Meili (time: twenty-six minutes and fifty-two seconds), (2) Shi Huizhi (last year's runner-up), (3) Yang Mali (last year's champion). (Children's Division) Champion: Guo Keming (time: seventeen minutes and fifty-two seconds, a remarkable 13th place overall), (2) Zhuang Mingzhi, (3) Li Da.

Educational News

Ministry of Education Orders Improvement of Four Universities in Hubei 152

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 13th) Based on inspection reports, the Ministry of Education issued an order on the 13th to National Wuhan University, Hubei Provincial Education College, Private Wuchang China University, and Huazhong University to earnestly improve their school affairs in accordance with the points listed in the order.

National Wuhan University (Beijing News) The Ministry of Education issued an order to Wuhan's public and private universities on the 13th to earnestly improve various aspects, the order is as follows: (1) The order to National Wuhan University states, "The Ministry has previously provided key points and ordered improvements. After reviewing the inspectors' reports, the university has conscientiously implemented the points suggested by the Ministry's order. Furthermore, efforts have been made in rationalizing the allocation of funds, expanding facilities, and improving teaching and examinations. However, the following points still need attention and compliance, to be reported for record: (1) The university's College of Agriculture is already established, and new students or short-term training courses should be enrolled in the coming year based on the faculty and facilities. Efforts should still be actively devoted to expanding and improving the facilities. (2) The university should find ways to enhance the teaching and research work of the Colleges of Science and Engineering. Professors should take more responsibility for guiding the science students' practical work and not completely delegate it to teaching assistants. The College of Engineering needs to recruit talented faculty to meet the needs of the college's development. (3) Student dormitories and clothing should be kept clean and tidy, and sloppiness should not be tolerated. The university's adoption of a mentor-like system for freshmen is very beneficial and should be implemented with care to maximize its effectiveness.

Hubei Provincial Education College (2) The order to Hubei Provincial Education College states, "The Ministry has previously provided key points and urged improvements. After reviewing the inspectors' reports, the college has only ordered the planning and implementation of vocational schools in the agricultural sciences, with little other improvement. The key points are re-emphasized below: (1) The college's curriculum should be practical, reducing education courses and increasing agricultural courses, with a particular emphasis on agricultural technology training. (2) Practice fields and equipment must be expanded. (3) Excellent faculty must be carefully selected for agriculture and other basic courses to improve teaching efficiency. Apart from matters concerning this year's enrollment, which have been separately instructed, you are hereby ordered to conscientiously comply and report."

Wuchang China University (3) The order to Private Wuchang China University states, "The Ministry has previously provided key points and urged improvements. According to the inspectors' reports, the university has made efforts in student management and examination procedures. The Department of Chemistry and the Applied Chemistry Department of the high school have also emphasized research and experimentation. However, the Dongshan campus has not been built, the foundation has not been further raised, and although books and instruments have been slightly added, the foundation is too poor and still insufficient. The number of staff is excessive, with office expenses accounting for 28%, which is considered excessive. Teachers lack specialization in the subjects they teach and often hold concurrent positions outside the university. The admission standards for new students are too lax, etc. After reviewing the reports, the university has made little improvement on the points suggested by the Ministry's orders in the past year. This year, all departments and courses except for Chemistry, Chinese Literature, Education, and Business Administration should suspend enrollment. The university should still follow the points below to vigorously rectify the situation, to observe future effects, and report the rectification situation in detail: (1) Start the construction of the new campus as soon as possible. (2) Actively raise foundation funds, with at least a considerable amount within the year. (3) Reduce office expenses and enrich the content of equipment. (4) Select and hire excellent and qualified full-time teachers, and strictly limit their concurrent teaching positions outside the university. (5) Raise the standards for admitting new students and strictly conduct entrance examinations."

Huazhong University (4) The order to Private Wuchang Huazhong University states, "The Ministry has previously provided key points and ordered improvements. After reviewing the inspection reports, the university has conscientiously implemented the points suggested by the Ministry's order. However, excellent faculty should be hired to teach courses such as Chinese Literature, Economics, Commerce, History, and Society. You are hereby ordered to comply with and improve."

Ministry of Education Re-Explains Regulations for Qualifying Teachers in Secondary and Normal Schools 153

The Ministry of Education replied to the Shandong Education Department regarding the regulations for qualifying teachers in secondary and normal schools, which was previously published in this newspaper. The Ministry's specific replies to the Shandong Education Department and the Shanghai Education Bureau regarding this matter are recorded below:

(1) The Ministry of Education, in response to a telegram from He Siyuan of the Shandong Education Department, stated that Article 4, (2), Item 1 of the regulations for qualifying secondary school teachers, "Does the specialist course refer specifically to the advanced normal school specialist course or also to the university specialist course? Furthermore, is there a difference in qualifications between specialist courses lasting two years and specialist courses lasting three years? Are they equivalent to specialist schools? Please advise." The Ministry of Education explained, "Article 4, (2), Item 2 of the provisional regulations for qualifying teachers in secondary and normal schools refers specifically to the advanced normal school specialist course. There is no difference in the qualification for certification between the two-year and three-year advanced normal school specialist courses, and the specialist course is equivalent to a specialist school. However, the certification should be handled in accordance with the certification regulations."

(2) The Ministry of Education replied to the Shanghai Education Bureau, stating that in Articles 4 and 5 of the provisional regulations for qualifying teachers in secondary and normal schools, the teaching experience of graduates from schools above the specialist level is not limited to any specific level of school, while the teaching experience of graduates from schools equivalent to senior high school should be limited to secondary schools.

Mr. Jin Zongcheng's Contribution to This Year's Students Studying Abroad 159

Mr. Jin Zongcheng published the following article yesterday, "A Humble Contribution to the Students Studying Abroad": In today's China, with its backward industry, declining commerce, and bankrupt rural areas, the atmosphere of recession pervades the globe, and it is especially severe in our country. Some commentators say that the key to recovery lies in the self-awareness and striving of the Chinese people. However, I place even greater hope in the students studying abroad. In recent years, every August and September, a large group of students has gone to study in various countries in Europe and America. This is because science has advanced rapidly in modern Europe and America, and everything is governed by scientific methods, leading to their prosperity today. You are going to study their applied sciences and contribute them to the nation and society after you have completed your studies, so that the country becomes strong. The mission you bear is heavy and great. As the ancient sage said, "When Heaven is about to place a great responsibility on someone, it first afflicts their mind, exhausts their muscles, and starves their body." This time, you students studying abroad will travel across the ocean. At best, it can enhance the international standing; at worst, it will study industry and commerce. The mission you bear is heavy and great. This is the beginning of shouldering great responsibility in the future. Although you have resources, you do not need to exhaust your muscles or starve your body. But if you want to study the practical knowledge of those countries and how they have prospered, you must suffer your mind. If your heart is not firm and your will is not strong, you will not succeed. If you are not dedicated, you will not learn anything essential, and you will not be able to use it unless you do practical work on the ground to learn how to implement the technology. You are all well-educated scholars in China, so there is no need for my superfluous words. However, I have read the Customs reports, and the amount of our country's annual trade deficit is alarming. Although this is the result of commercial competition among various countries, it is also a reflection of the Chinese people's fondness for foreign goods and their disregard for domestic goods. You students studying abroad, whether in commerce or industry, should follow your inclinations and study the reasons for our country's alarming trade deficit, why foreign goods are sold in our country, and why Chinese people despise domestic goods, in addition to your academic studies. You must research the root cause and prepare for future reforms. In a few years, when you return home and dedicate yourselves to society, all aspects of our country that are insufficient to compete with others will rely on you to use your knowledge to build the foundation, or transform it to serve those who could not study abroad. Therefore, you are going abroad to study today, and you will be the masters of transforming China in the future. Your responsibility is heavy and great, and the people of the country have high expectations for you. I dare to offer my sincere words and ask you to work hard for the motherland.

Little Boy (10) (3) 165

— Original by American Ms. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

In that bathroom, there were two large basins, as well as foot basins, spray tubes, and various washing facilities. Ned was soon immersed in another basin, the water was warm and comfortable! At the same time, he watched two women wipe four or five small children clean, put them in white, clean pajamas, and then they curled up in bed. As for the few children, they wanted to play many tricks at the same time, making everyone seem to be caught in a whirlwind of laughter until they were suffocated in their beds.

Ned washed his body, wrapped himself well in a blanket, and sat next to the stove. Nasui cut his hair for him, and then another group of children came and were locked in the bathroom. Only the sound of splashing water could be heard inside, like a group of little whales playing.

"Ned should still lie here. This way, when he coughs at night, you can give him a lot of sesame seed juice to drink," said Madam Pei. She ran around, like a hen busy taking care of a large group of restless chicks.

Nasui agreed with the plan, immediately put Ned in a flannel pajama, gave him some warm and sweet things to drink, and then wrapped him in one of the two beds in the room. He lay in bed, like a serene and full mummy, feeling that he had enjoyed all the happiness in the world. Cleanliness itself is a fresh and pleasant feeling; in his world, flannel pajamas had never been heard of; a few comforting words moisturized his desolate heart; a few sips of "good stuff" calmed his cough, the pleasure was the same; and the feeling of being cared for made the simple room look like a paradise to the homeless child. This was like a sweet dream. He closed his eyes repeatedly to test whether this situation would disappear after opening them. Since it proved that this was not an illusion, the joy made it even more difficult for him to fall asleep, even if he tried to fall asleep, it was still impossible, because in these few minutes, a strange system of Plum Village was presented to his astonished but appreciative eyes.

Yellow Millet Dream and Wanghua Fort 167

— Sun Shouchang

Old classmate Huang Xinyi is recently in Handan. Because of the story of the Yellow Millet Dream, which originated in that county, I sent a letter asking him to inquire about the origin of this matter nearby. Yesterday, I received a letter from him, describing it in detail, which I transcribe below to inform readers. The following is all what Mr. Huang said:

Huangliangmeng is a town in Handan County, Hebei. It was originally named Wanghua Fort. It is famous for Li Bi's "Pillow Book," which describes Lu Sheng's Yellow Millet Dream. Over time, the true name was hidden. Today, most people call the town Huangliangmeng directly and no longer know the old name, except that the Pinghan Railway passes through here and sets up a station, still named Wanghua Fort. According to what is recorded in the Pillow Book, it roughly says: "There was a Lu Sheng who was keen on wealth and honor, and had not made a name for himself even in his prime. He was very depressed. One day, he met Old Man Lu at an inn. The old man was cooking yellow millet and gave Lu Sheng a pillow, saying, 'Pillow on this and you will be able to get what you want.' Lu Sheng received the pillow, and soon dreamed of passing the imperial examination, marrying a daughter of the Cui family of Boling, whose daughter was very beautiful. From then on, his career became prominent, and he served as a general and prime minister for decades, with mansions connected to the clouds, enjoying the pleasures of life to the fullest, unaware that he was in a dream. By one night, he died of old age and illness, and his dream suddenly woke up. He saw Old Man Lu was beside him, and the yellow millet he was cooking was not yet cooked." As for whether this record is a fact or an allegory, I am not a person in the dream, so I dare not make a dogmatic judgment. However, just from the wonderful intention of this article and the depth of its touching people, it is not necessary for there to be a true immortal or a true dream. The author is already endowed with immortal bones. Pu Liuxian wrote "Continuation of the Yellow Millet Dream" in "Liaozhai," venting his anger for a while. The depiction is extremely detailed, but it becomes a dog's tail. This spring, I happened to travel to Handan and had the good fortune to visit this scenic spot. The town is twelve miles away from the city. The ruins of that year have now been built as the Lu Weng Temple, with the gate facing the Yanzhao thoroughfare. The plaque on the temple reads "Handan Ancient Temple." Inside the gate, there is a high wall with stone carvings embedded in it, with the four characters "Fairyland on Penglai" written in large characters. The strokes are agile and seem to fly and come alive. It is said to be the immortal's brush. Further in is the main hall, where a statue of Lu Xian is enshrined in the middle, dressed in Confucian robes and carrying a sword, with a chic and unrestrained air, no less than the demeanor of a scholar. Looking at it, one cannot help but feel leisurely, making people want to transcend the world. In front of the main hall, turn left to another courtyard, with ten acres of ponds, winding bridges and blue railings, pavilions and towers, quiet and secluded, quite worth a visit. Near the pool, there is another high-built hall, where a statue of Han Zhongli is enshrined in the middle, with a huge belly and staring eyes, not only without any immortal energy, but directly close to the demonic path. The Taoist priest told me: "Mr. Zhongli is the teacher of Lu Xian, so he is enshrined together." I said: "Since you enshrine the teacher of Lu Xian here, you should also enshrine the disciple of Lu Xian. I know that Lu Xian has a high disciple, a willow tree spirit. Why is he absent today, not allowing him to be compared to the four配十哲 of Xuan Ni, which is unfair." The Taoist priests all laughed. Behind this hall is the Lu Sheng Temple, said to be the place where yellow millet was cooked in the inn that year. Now a sleeping statue of Lu Sheng is enshrined inside. The statue is carved from a whole block of huge stone, connected to the base, as large as a human body, wearing a Confucian scarf and robes, supporting one arm with a pillow and sleeping, and still not awake. Judging from its stone carvings, it is exquisite and not cleverly woven, probably relics of the Song and Jin dynasties. All those who come here to pay tribute to this sleeping statue cannot help but stroke and feel emotional, lingering and unwilling to leave. Over the years, the statue has become dark and smooth, and the light can reflect people. There are very few steles in Handan, but this temple alone has many stone carvings, all of which are poems by famous people of past dynasties, embedded all over the walls, with almost no gaps. Reading them, there are many famous lines. Because their feelings are so deep, their words are often filled with deep feelings. The scenery moves people, to such an extent that I have been busy in the world for a long time and have abandoned chanting. Here, I also feel something, and poetic meaning arises spontaneously. On the way back, I got a seven-character quatrain: "Cooking cooked yellow millet has been allowed for a long time, I come to borrow a pillow, I am afraid it is too late, I know I do not have the blessings of gods, dare to raise a glass to Mr. Zhizhi." It is said that Lu Xian once got drunk in Yueyang, and I also have the same habit. As for the so-called yellow millet, it is the millet of today. To this day, the residents of Handan still use this to cook rice, and the rice is yellow, so it is called yellow millet."

The War Atmosphere Manufacturing Industry 168

Water Carrier 169

— Yun Su

"One monk carries water to eat, two monks carry water together, and three monks have no water to eat"; this describes the lazy habits of dependent people. The more people there are, the lower the work efficiency is. In fact, this refers to employees who are paid monthly. If the amount of water carried is used as the standard for obtaining compensation, everyone will have a heart to move upwards; the water carrier is a kind of labor, which is no less than iron making, rowing boats, and grinding tofu, which are considered the most hard work by everyone in ancient and modern China; iron making, rowing boats, and grinding tofu are operations that take place day and night, and carrying water is a pore of sweat beads, just like half a catty versus eight taels; there is tap water in the city, so you don’t need this hard work. In small cities in the interior, stove houses and bathhouses are their major customers, and every household cannot do without their traces. They are afraid of continuous rain, and everyone stores "sky water", and they are in danger of starving! Every year, I look forward to a "warm water field" because with drinking water, you also need water. This summer's "warm water field" is their golden age; residents close to the public river sell two copper plates for a burden of water, but the water in the city is precious. The porters don’t have such long shoulder strength. Carrying two buckets of water will spill half a bucket, so the people in the city are water pushers: Seeing that there is a jade belt river, it’s just like the restaurants Lou Wai Lou and Tian Wai Tian on West Lake, just deceiving people. Self-flowing wells are not available to every household, so water carriers have become a specialized profession: "Xiao Dazi", the water carrier on our street, is known to everyone. He is from Taiping Hall, Yangzhou County. His voice is particularly clear and crisp. Everyone laughs when they see him and says: "Xiao Dazi", sing one. He doesn't put on airs, and hums along. He has read the Thousand Character Classic and can sing the seven-character couplets of Liang Shanbo and Zhu Yingtai. He is afraid that someone will mistakenly change his water bucket, so he wrote six large characters "Xiao Dazi" "Xiao Dazi" on both sides of the bucket. This seems to be his invincible trademark; he eats thousands of meals, uses hundreds of dollars, and is naked in the spring, summer and autumn. He occasionally wears a white short shirt and pants and old cloth shoes and socks that are washed in Hunan, and he loses his true face. Naughty children, when they see him, find fun and say: Xiao Dazi, are you a groom!

Records of Drifting Fragrance of Imperial Incense 170

— Original by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The more the lotus flowers bloom, the more intense the fragrance becomes.

The little birds also smelled the fragrance, and flew over from all directions, flying low over the pile of lotus bushes: their wings kept beating in the air, and a magical effect occurred, that is, the fragrance of the lotus flowers was blown over by them, so it was particularly easy for us to smell it.

The sun rose higher and higher, and the light gradually became stronger, and everything on the lake was revealed by the sunlight.

Now we can see the pink stamens in those lotus flowers! - But at this time they have not yet fully opened, and still retain the original color of the buds. They seem to be waiting for something, just revealing the fragrance to the fullest, and still unwilling to fully reveal their appearance.

"Ah! What an interesting and wonderful scene!" The Old Buddha said to herself again. "And a wonderful scene full of vitality! Only at this time can people feel the beauty and loveliness of nature, and know that everything that has life has a considerable relationship with us humans..."

Her voice was very low and soft, and the following words were simply ambiguous; originally she herself had realized that the previous few words were really too awkward and too unreasonable, so she deliberately made them ambiguous. In fact, none of us paid attention to her words. Everyone had been deceived by their eyes, thinking that so many lotus flowers were blooming at the same time, there must be a wonderful sound to be heard, so everyone on the boat was like me, leaning their ears to listen carefully to the "lotus sound". (389)

World Wonders

— (Bingyu)

The world's oldest potato

In Mather Dante Village, Australia, the world's oldest potato was recently discovered. This potato belongs to Ulta, Ma Meli. According to Mr. Wu, it was left over from cooking by his grandmother when the first generation immigrated to this village. So, it has been 133 years now. Because this potato was placed on the stove shelf, no one knew about it. Later, it was heated and smoked, and gradually hardened, like red stone. After his grandmother died, she left this thing to his father. When his father left it, he said that this thing had been 83 years old. Now Mr. Wu has lived for another 60 years. Calculated together, it is indeed 133 years, which is a worldwide antique unseen.

The world's number one tea drinker

In Bengal, India, there is a man named Nai Baer·Qiang Tella·Bai Tai Zhi Er, who is 48 years old this year. Since he was 18 years old, on average, he has drunk 300,000 cups of black tea. Now he still drinks three or four times a day, each time drinking at least five or six cups, and up to ten cups. Statistics show that he drinks 20 cups a day, but his appearance is like a person in his thirties, so some people say that drinking more black tea can make you live forever.

The world's largest rough gem

There is a gem merchant in New York named Harry Winston, who bought a stone containing small gems for 900,000 yuan. This stone was discovered by an old man named Yun Jia, who is already 60 years old, in the Da Bai Lai Mia mine. It weighs 3,100 carats and contains 100 small gems, two of which are very large. It is currently being processed.

The world's most beef-loving country

The most beef-eating people in the world are New Zealanders, followed by Englishmen. New Zealanders eat an average of 90 kilograms per person per year, followed by Australia, and then Argentina (one kilogram is 26 taels in our country, and 90 kilograms is about 150 catties in our country).

The country with the most telephones in the world

The total number of telephones in the world is 35.5 million. The United States accounts for half, European countries account for one-third, and Asia accounts for only 3% of the United States, which is less than 1,065,000. Japan has the most in Asia, estimated at 950,000. According to our country's statistics, there are 50,000.

The place with the least rainfall in the world

In Asyan, in the Nile River basin, it was originally a land without rain. A few years ago, there was a sudden flood. The natives were surprised to see the rain. Near Arica Bay in Chile, South America, it never rains. The average annual rainfall in this coastal area is one millimeter, and as little as 0.5 millimeters. Conversely, the place with the most rainfall in the world is Manaulan on the ancient Hengshan Mountain northeast of Calcutta, India, with an annual rainfall of 12,665 millimeters.

The world's only large Buddhist prayer beads

Since the birth of Sakyamuni Buddha, it has been 2,500 years. On Mount Rokko in Hyogo Prefecture, Japan, there is a memorial tower with a circle of large Buddhist beads surrounding the waist of the tower. There are 84,000 beads, about 2,600 meters long and weighing 12,375 kilograms, making them the world's only large Buddhist prayer beads.

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 17 Don't Ask About a Daughter's Identity, Difficult to Speak Hidden Pain, Strive to See a Noble Person's Face, and Admire a High Style Together

Huanhua blushed and stood up and said, "Then, I am really grateful." Saying that, she bowed and left. He walked out of the room, and still heard Zhiqian sigh. The gold market yesterday initially showed a weakening trend due to the efforts of major players to actively sell, leading to strong selling pressure.
