Recovery of the Kuling British Concession 184

— Xing An

The long-negotiated matter of recovering the Kuling British Concession has now come to a conclusion. On the 8th of this month, our representative Jiang Zhicheng and British Consul-General Moss jointly signed the agreement. The content of the agreement is as follows: (1) Return the land lease of the British concession of 1905 to our country; (2) The public utilities within the original concession will be managed by the Chinese government; (3) British residents in Kuling may establish an advisory committee for Chinese consultation, but our country has the final decision-making power on matters of consultation. This recovery of the concession involves four locations: (1) Changhang, (2) Yishengwa, (3) Caodipo, (4) Dalianchong, all of which are scenic spots in Kuling.

The existence of a British concession in Kuling may no longer be noticed by our countrymen. Therefore, the recovery of this concession this time may not arouse our excitement. But this is indeed the result of our country's diplomatic efforts. For an independent country, it must have autonomy over all its territory, even the smallest inch. Therefore, the recovery of the Kuling British Concession must be regarded as a matter worth celebrating.

However, the recovery of the Kuling British Concession has even greater significance. It makes it clear to all countries that our country is determined to recover concessions. The negotiation and recovery of the Kuling British Concession is only the first step in our country's diplomatic work. In the future, we hope that concessions in various places can also be continuously recovered. This is precisely the right that our country should have.

Perhaps some people say that it is easy to recover the concession land in Kuling, but it is difficult to recover the concession land in other places. The reason why Britain is willing to return the Kuling concession is because the Kuling concession is not very important and can only be used for summer resorts. If it is the Shanghai International Settlement, which is the economic center of the British in the Far East, it would not be easy for them to give it up. This is indeed true. However, this time Britain returned the Kuling concession, although it was willing to give it up because the Kuling concession was not important. But this is also considered a kind of goodwill from a friendly country. In the future, if our government authorities can make further efforts at appropriate times, it is not absolutely impossible to recover concessions in various places.

The Seashore of Tangjiawan 185

— Ai Tu

With a heart full of remembrance, and with a pleasant breath, I once again boarded the car, quickly heading to the famous Tangjiawan for a stroll. As the car sped towards the southeast, I felt as if my body was passing through high mountains, and there was no end to the beautiful rural scenery to see. Unfortunately, the car was traveling so fast that it was just a fleeting "riding a horse and watching flowers." Before long, we could see the sea to the southeast from the carriage. That was the sea of Tangjiawan. The vast sea, illuminated by the evening sun, was a sweeping arc, unfolding far and wide, with gently drifting white waves reflecting the golden sunlight, turning into a beautiful color picture, covering everything on the sea. A few small warships and many merchant ships were sparsely moored in the center of the sea.

When the car took us to the seaside, we could breathe in the fresh sea breeze and hear the soft sound of the waves crashing against the rocks, the white waves thrown out, scattering into the sky.

Arriving at Tangjiawan, the site of the Zhongshan County Government, I had always fantasized that it would be magnificent, with good architecture and commerce. However, it was simply empty, a dilapidated small city, the coldness of commerce so pitiful, not even one-tenth of Shiqi. Everything gave us a sense of dread, only decay. Especially in recent years, the impact of political changes has created seeds of misfortune everywhere.

On the roads and small streets, we couldn't see any particularly good buildings, and the roads were sometimes bumpy and difficult to drive on. All the images were desolate and bleak. All of this couldn't help but disappoint me.

Wandering alone on the seashore, strolling at the foot of the mountain, my mood was so desolate – I carried many desolate shadows, moving with everything in the dusk. Yes, I always have many, many dreams when I wander on such journeys. When I stared at the small warships moored on the vast sea, I seemed to see a terrible war about to break out there. Yes, this is a very good county, but I don't know how many people are treating the people as expendable, engaging in extreme deception and exploitation. How terrible! The peaceful countryside has long been engulfed in man-eating shadows, and it's no wonder that everything here is so desolate and bleak.

The colors of dusk have gradually become dark and terrifying.

The vast bay is also covered with a terrifying curtain, but everything is still silent. There is no noisy sound in the market, no atmosphere of a big city, gradually buried in the circle of death, and people are gradually going to sleep.

However, I am still wandering alone on the seashore, breathing in the sea breeze, trying to find some comforting scenery on this silent seashore. But everything is hidden in the god of the night, with terrifying claws everywhere, the shadows swaying. The sea's answer to me is only the sound of the waves crashing, revealing a certain tone. Other than that, nothing can be heard.

When I returned to my lodging in the market with weariness, many people were already quiet, only the pale yellow lights on the street were still flickering desolately. Indeed, once night falls, everything in Tangjiawan is already buried in the circle of death.

Beside the Train Tracks 186

— Fang Qin

When my hazy, bloated head is raised towards the vast and boundless blue sky, and I gaze at the thousands of miles of floating white clouds, I seem to be startled and ask myself: "How do I live every day?" It feels like a moment of awakening, filled with disappointment and loss. But after a while, my mood sinks to who knows where, and I lower my heavy head.

I've moved more than ten times recently, and I don't even know what's going on. I just feel restless, like a bird that can't find a nest to settle in. A bed, a small table, a suitcase, a chair, moving them back and forth, only seeing them get damaged, and seeing myself getting thinner. It's as if my home has become a child who doesn't know how to live.

This time, I moved to Jiangwan, a village. In the fiery torrent, I escaped from the steamer-like small pavilion and came here to experience some cool breeze that seems to have no owner. I began to relax a few breaths, and sometimes in the evening, sitting in front of the door, welcoming the gentle breeze, I even felt a slight awakening of life. However, that moment of awakening disappeared quickly, and it seemed like a long time since I had been cut off from the cool breeze; although the cool breeze blows morning and evening, floating the light silk sleeves of people who are relaxed and the freely swaying leaves. It can't blow away the endless accumulation of my heavy, swollen, hot, and numb chest and brain!

Sometimes, I catch a glimpse of the green grass in front, the secluded shady place, where girls and boys are taking leisurely, indulgent, and pleasant strolls, chatting, singing softly, indulging in beautiful and vast reveries, and wandering freely and lightly. I can't help but wonder suddenly: Why am I always living such a depressed life for no reason? I can spend my days like them, and be as happy as them. However, as soon as this thought arrives, it disappears, and I am still my depressed self. Even if I want to go, I don't know how to make it happen even once. As for the park I envy, I often dream of being able to immerse myself in the cool, secluded green forest every day, which would at least be good for my wounded body and mind. Who knew that after saving a dollar to buy a park ticket, I never actually went in.

I not only don't know why this is, but the thought of it only increases my depression!

Is my life forever like a nightmare?

In front of my house, two railway tracks stretch out windingly. I live a lonely, isolated, and painful life beside these train tracks. At first, I was always blank and silent towards them. And the sharp cries of the trains that constantly run over the tracks make me very disgusted and angry. Their sharp cries irritate my brain and make me even more uneasy.

But once, when my angry eyes followed a train as it sped forward like thunder and lightning, the heroic, speedy, mighty, and forward posture awakened me and made me marvel with joy, a surge of emotion welling up. The spring of my heart, which had passed away, is running again! My life suddenly feels awakened! I am immersed in clear reminiscence. I discover that only at this moment am I truly awake! This is what can keep me from being numb!

Therefore, the piercing cries of the trains no longer make me resentful. Every time a cruel nightmare awakens me from the dark middle of the night! I often get up, open the door, and go out. I watch the trains speeding forward, and under the quiet night through which the trains have passed, I feel the magnificence and vastness of the surrounding night scenery make me happy. The cool night breeze finally blows all over my body, making me even more awake. Standing quietly, I am calm and excited, and I feel some fullness of life. I am just now discovering my own existence!

Page 18

Lodging in a Desolate Village at Dusk (Continued) 187

— Xin Ye

"Well! Our boat is docked at the cement factory pier outside the city. It's about a dozen miles away from the city. This area is all countryside, so I don't know if there's any place to get a meal." The boat owner replied to me like this.

The sun had set, and although the boat was still moving forward in this vast expanse of misty waves, my heart was as heavy as if it were filled with a thousand pieces of lead.

When the boat reached the pier, a crescent moon had quietly hidden overhead, emitting a charming soft light. I jumped ashore and shouted "Goodbye" to the people on the boat, but in my heart, I was actually quite hesitant. I couldn't think of a solution, so I had to follow the boat owner's instructions and walk along the road to the east. Fortunately, the moonlight that night was very bright, so I could still make out the direction and the road.

Dragging a lonely shadow, walking on this dark road like a ghost, I couldn't help but feel a little apprehensive. The village dogs were barking incessantly, and I really didn't know what to do!

"Wouldn't it be better to inquire about Xu Village and stay overnight at my cousin's house and then figure things out? Anyway, I'm not familiar with the area, and it's inconvenient to travel at night." In my desperation, I came up with an idea and remembered that there was a forgotten cousin here, so I planned to stay there for the night.

So, I knocked on a door by the road and asked for directions to Xu Village!

Xu Village was such a desolate and isolated village, not connected to any other village to the front, back, left, or right. I asked several families in a row, asked many questions, and said "I'm sorry" countless times before I finally found my cousin's house.

That cousin was a lonely old woman. Her uncle had passed away long ago, and she had no cousins, but she had managed to save some money in her hands, so she could live out her lonely old age peacefully! When she saw her cousin, whom she hadn't seen in three years, how she squinted her old, presbyopic eyes in welcome!

That night, I lay in bed, tossing and turning and unable to fall asleep, just staring blankly at the ray of moonlight that shone in through the window hole; staring blankly at the four walls, the room was empty and I couldn't help but feel a little scared.

Later, I finally fell asleep because I was too tired, so I don't know when I fell asleep. When I woke up, I saw the sun had slipped into the room. At that time, my cousin was standing at the door of the room with a smile:

"Cousin, you're up early! Sleep a little longer!"

But I had to do my own business, and it would be too much to fail her kind hospitality. (The End)

Entering the City 188

— Lu Sun

When the sky was just showing a sliver of white on the skylight, A Cui rolled out of the tattered bedding. But in this damp bedroom, it was still as dark as hell: the light from the skylight could only illuminate a few inches. So A Cui opened her eyes wide, like a wild cat, trying to find her object. She tiptoed out of bed and felt a soft piece of clothing on a three-legged stool. The touch of her fingers told her that it was the patterned cloth jacket that she had been looking forward to day and night.

The darkness seemed to release some light, and she quickly put it on. Using the light coming in from the skylight, she wanted to take a look at her own reflection in the small mirror on the wall. Although it didn't reflect a flower-like beauty as she had imagined, she could only vaguely see the spots of the patterned fabric in the tofu-sized frame. Even so, she felt that the body wrapped in the patterned fabric was a beautiful, reborn person.

So she laughed, uncontrollably, but it woke up her parents in their sleep.

The bedroom was gradually brightening, and when A Cui's parents saw their daughter wearing the new jacket, yesterday's events were brought up again in their two old hearts. Such a young daughter, but given to the Zhou village elder for no reason? But thinking about the years of unpaid rent, the old father couldn't help but shed tears. Just because of that one reason, owing rent to Zhou village elder, he couldn't consider his daughter's lifelong happiness.

Yesterday, A Cui's father was summoned away by the bailiff in the morning and didn't return home until sunset. He looked as if he had done a day's hard labor, and couldn't even stand up straight when he walked. As soon as he entered the door, he lay on the bed like a lazy ox, ignoring anyone's questions, as if the questioners were his enemies. He stared at the mother and daughter with bloodshot eyes. The daughter had already started crying, thinking that her father was seriously ill in her weak heart, because her father had never been like that before.

The elderly mother already knew what was going on: the bailiff was never a good person. Whenever he came to the door, it meant bad luck for someone. A Cui's father had been summoned for the whole day, so it couldn't be anything good. But she didn't expect that the bad thing would fall on her daughter.

The matter was like this: when the father with bloodshot eyes told them about the deadline set by the bailiff, the mother couldn't hold back her tears any longer. She stamped her bound feet and cursed, cursing Zhou village elder for being a bloodsucker; cursing the bailiff, that dog, for always offering him big fish and meat on holidays, but ending up helping that demon to plot against her own daughter. So she felt as if her daughter was about to be taken away and hugged her into her arms. But the daughter didn't know what they were arguing about. Her mother often cried, so it must be someone forcing her to give them money. She looked around the simple bedroom carefully and knew that the valuable things had been taken away. So her eyes fell on the new foreign-made cloth jacket, which her father hadn't had time to pawn today because that dog was forcing her father to leave. She naively told her mother to use it to pay off the debt, and that she could go hungry for a few days.

"What good would that do!" The mother scolded, but she immediately understood that her daughter knew that there wasn't a single penny left in the house. She thought that this jacket could pay off her father's debts. She hugged her daughter even tighter and said softly with tears in her eyes: "This jacket can't be given to anyone. You put it on, and your father will take you to the city tomorrow."

The old man's eyes were still bloodshot, and the new patterned jacket seemed like a man-eating leopard in front of him, about to snatch away his daughter. But what could he do? He owed people money.

Is Sister Sa, Really Sa? 195

"Sister Sa, are you really Sa?"

Most people, upon seeing Cang Yinqiu, nicknamed "Sister Sa," would have this question in their minds, wanting to ask Cang Yinqiu directly. However, the words would reach their throats and then be swallowed back. No one has ever dared to ask Cang Yinqiu such a question, fearing that she would turn her face and not recognize them, resulting in an embarrassing situation. Thus, whether Cang Yinqiu is really "Sa" remains a question. Because unless she personally admits it publicly, it cannot be established.

The reason Cang Yinqiu has the nickname "Sister Sa" may seem like an insult to those who don't understand the details, a public defamation. But in reality, it is high praise for Madam Cang because her "silly" performance in "Human Fairy" achieved valuable success, hence the nickname. Madam Cang also understands and has never refused the bestowal of "Sister Sa," but she has also never admitted to it, perhaps out of "self-deprecation"?

Because Madam Cang is unwilling to clearly express her acceptance or rejection of the "Sister Sa" nickname, people want to ask Madam Cang face-to-face, "Sister Sa, are you really Sa?" But people are also timid and dare not ask.

Yuan Congmei is very clever. He accurately grasped people's psychology and specially, in his directed sound film "Storm," called on Madam Cang to personally answer people's question about her: are you "Sister Sa"? If you want Madam Cang to answer your long-standing question, just go and see the premiere of the "Storm" sound film, and you will understand.

Pay attention! "Storm" is about to be released.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Automotive Weekly

A Major Innovation in the Automotive World Rear-Engine Car Successfully Tested 198

— Yu

Currently, the common cars we are accustomed to all have the engine installed in the front. The engine's power propels the entire car forward. The most important part of the car is installed at the front. If the front of the car collides with something due to careless driving, and the engine is damaged, the entire car will be immobilized and unable to move forward. In recent years, car manufacturers have ingeniously researched moving the engine to the rear. After several field tests and reforms, this so-called rear-engine car has been a great success. Its various advantages, such as stability and fuel efficiency, are fascinating. This can be described as a major innovation in automobile manufacturing. The following describes the driving situation of America's first rear-engine car, the "Scarab," and the ironclad proof of the successful testing of this rear-engine car.

This rear-engine car, dubbed "the car of tomorrow," the "Scarabb," was introduced to the automotive world by its inventor, William Stout, four months ago. Now, due to its performance results, it has proven to be an absolute success. This rear-engine car was originally unknown and obscure. It was not until February of this year, when its creator, Stout, came forward to introduce it and greet people in the automotive industry, that it began to attract attention. Since that first appearance, this "Scarabb" has been driven by its owner every day, braving the wind and rain. Unconsciously, more than four months have passed. In these 120-plus days, the roads it has traveled are also truly impressive. According to its owner's calculation, it has traveled over 22,000 miles. In this long journey of 22,000 miles, it has passed through good and bad roads of all kinds. Moreover, the weather and environment in different places are completely different. It can be said that every place has its own unique flavor. On average, it travels about 500 miles per day. The speed is 60 miles per hour when fast and 55 miles per hour when slow. Overall, in the daily mileage of more than 500 miles, the speed per hour is around 50 or 60 miles, which cannot be said to be as slow as a snail climbing a wall.

In this preliminary test, according to Stout, the inventor of the "Scarabb," the fuel consumption is extremely economical. The total fuel consumption is only 20 quarts, and on average, one gallon of gasoline can travel 18 miles. Stout was encouraged by this initial success and decided to build 100 cars within this year, and then continue to manufacture and sell them. According to a report from the end of June in Detroit, the "Scarabb's" second version will be born in July. It is also reported that once it is fully equipped, it will also undergo thorough testing on various roads like its older brother. The braking part of the car is hydraulically controlled.

Stout's first test journey was from Detroit to Florida and back to the starting point. During this journey, the "Scarabb" only needed one nail of water for cooling in the engine. The second journey still started from Detroit, passed through Los Angeles to Seattle, and then returned to its starting point - Detroit. This Stout and his companions were really enjoying themselves. They sat in the car as if they were traveling in a comfortable compartment. At night, the movable seat could be disassembled and moved to form a bed, so they could sleep comfortably in the car. They not only ate in the car, but also drank coffee for entertainment after meals. At this time, the coffee cups in the compartment, and the liquid inside, did not spill out at all.

When the "Scarabb" passed through the western states, the wind was very strong. But thanks to the streamlined shape of the car body, it did not feel uncomfortable at all. When passing through Kansas City, it encountered a dust devil. The dust filled the air, making it impossible to see the scenery. They had no choice but to sigh and complain. They were confined to a hotel by the dust storm, unable to move a step. It was not until the dust in the room had slightly subsided and they could barely see things clearly outside the three storefronts that they added some oil to the car's engine. The windows and vents were tightly closed to prevent the dust storm from invading. According to Stout's later account, "There was less dust inside the car than in the hotel room," which is also thought-provoking.

Because the engine of the rear-engine car is installed at the back, the power comes from behind, making it extremely easy and effortless to climb hills. Moreover, because of the sharp modification of the car body, it is easy to see from any angle. During this test journey, the exhaust emissions from the engine and the heat generated by the radiator were reduced. Stout said that this was due to the rear-engine installation.

Some say that automobile king Henry Ford is very concerned and interested in this rear-engine "Scarabb" car. Stout said, "That has nothing to do with it, although sometimes I think it would be best if there was." The entire "Scarabb" looks like a beetle, entirely made of tubular fine steel welded together. According to Stout, it is even stronger than a Pullman car body.

The ventilation system in the car is a direct-flow system, allowing air to flow smoothly from the front to the back. The car body is fully insulated, and even the windows are fitted with special heat-insulating glass. Stout estimates that all American car factories will be manufacturing this type of rear-engine car in the next three years.

Several Simple Formulas Regarding Car Engines 199

— Lu

1. Cylinder Volume (Piston displacement)

The so-called cylinder volume, also known as displacement, refers to the volume of space that the piston passes through during each stroke. The stroke referred to here is the distance the piston travels from the inside to the outside or from the outside to the inside. It can also be said to be the distance the piston travels when the crank moves from top dead center to bottom dead center, or from bottom dead center to top dead center. If we already know the cylinder bore and stroke, the cylinder volume is not difficult to calculate. When we want to express the size of an engine, we should omit the words cylinder bore and stroke and only write two numbers. For example, 4.4 represents the cylinder bore, and 5 represents the stroke. Thus, a 4.4-5 engine means an engine with a 4-inch bore and a 5-inch stroke.

The cylinder volume of an engine is equal to the volume of one cylinder multiplied by the number of cylinders in the engine. This can be expressed by the following formula:

In the United States, cars are graded according to horsepower. This horsepower is calculated by formulas set by the Association of Licensed Automobile Manufacturers and the Society of Automotive Engineers. The horsepower calculated by this formula is not necessarily the correct horsepower under all circumstances, nor is it theoretically correct power. However, it is used to compare different engines.

This formula is derived from the formula for calculating the horsepower of steam engines. The formula for calculating the horsepower of steam engines is:

This formula is specifically for single-cylinder steam engines, and each stroke of the piston is a power stroke. To make this formula suitable for calculating the power of four-stroke car engines, it must be multiplied by the number of cylinders in the engine. Furthermore, since there is only one power stroke in a four-stroke engine, it must be divided by four. Thus, the formula for calculating the horsepower of a four-stroke engine is as follows:

To apply this formula to car engines, it has been determined that the piston speed is an average of 1,000 feet per minute, the average pressure is 10 pounds per square inch, and the mechanical efficiency is 75 percent. Substituting these values into the formula above, we get:

Modern engines have piston speeds that far exceed 1,000 feet per minute. If we calculate the ratio between the actual piston speed and the assumed piston speed, and then multiply this ratio by the horsepower calculated from the above formula, the result obtained will not be far from the power actually generated. To illustrate this point, let's still use the example above. The piston stroke is five and a half inches, and the crankshaft rotates 2,400 revolutions per minute. The piston speed is equal to the number of feet the piston travels per two revolutions multiplied by the number of revolutions per minute. In this case, the piston travels five and a half inches per stroke, and the crankshaft travels eleven inches per revolution. Then, at a speed of 2,400 revolutions, the piston will travel per minute:

This horsepower number is very close to the power actually generated by the engine.

American Automotive Tidbits 200

— Xiao Lian

A Large Revenue for the U.S. Government: According to statistics from U.S. government statisticians, the total number of various automobiles registered in the United States in 1934 was 24,933,403. These more than 20 million automobiles paid a total of $304,928,000 in registration fees and other miscellaneous fees to the government in the past three years. This is indeed a large revenue for the U.S. government.

A Glimmer of Prosperity in the Automotive Industry: The Pierce-Arrow car factory has been affected by the economic downturn in recent years. Its car factory in Evansville, Indiana, had already been closed due to downsizing. Recently, due to increased sales of Pierce-Arrow cars, the company's management has decided to restore the factory. They are currently assembling machinery and expect to start work in July or August of this year. The factory has been closed for three years. This restoration may be a small sign of prosperity in the American automotive industry.

Ford's Reforms for Next Year: Henry Ford, the boss of Ford Motor Company, recently stated informally that the appearance of Ford cars for next year (1936) will not undergo major changes. He said this entirely for the sake of car buyers. Because many people who bought cars this year will not feel that their car's style will become outdated next year. Therefore, the new Ford of next year will at most be improved in terms of internal components, while the appearance will remain the same. Ford's move, although ostensibly for the sake of buyers, is ultimately to generate more business for himself. After he said this, he can sell at least tens of thousands more cars this year.

Hudson Factory News 201

— Yun

8,800 Employees Hired at the Beginning of the Year

Plan to Produce 100,000 Cars

According to news from Detroit, Michigan, Hudson Motor Car Company had a total of 8,800 employees at the start of work this year, an increase of 60 percent compared to the 5,500 employees on the first day of work in 1934. According to the company's plan for the production of Hudson and Terraplane cars in 1935, the total output will be more than 100,000 vehicles. In 1934, the total output was only 86,000 vehicles.

In order to implement this new production plan, the company's expenditure on materials and other items will inevitably increase. It is estimated that the annual expenditure on this item will reach more than 40 million yuan. Among them, steel will be the largest expenditure, followed by rubber tires, textiles, castings, wheels, starting components, lighting equipment, ignition equipment, and carriages, glass, and wireless radios. According to the company's planned production for 1935, it will be the largest amount in any year since 1930. The total export volume in 1930 was 113,898 vehicles.
